```
18th +6 Integrated Cloaking d12 18 + 3
19th +6 Ability Score Improvement d12 19 + 3
20th +6 Perfect Body d12 20 + 3
```
##### Integrated Weapon

At 1st level, you can integrate up to two weapons into your body. You can integrate a
weapon over the course of 1 hour, which can be done during a short rest. The weapon
must be within your reach, and you integrate it into your body at the end of 1 hour. You
can't integrate weapons with the two-handed property into your body. While the
weapon is integrated, you gain the following benefits:

```
⦁ You can unsheathe one or more of your integrated weapons as part of the Attack
action on your turn, and you do not need a free hand to wield an integrated
weapon.
⦁ When you sheathe the weapon, it is undetectable by normal means.
⦁ While you are conscious, your integrated weapons can’t be removed from your
body against your will.
```
You can remove an integrated weapon over the course of 1 minute.

At 9th level, you can integrate up to 3 weapons into your body. At 13th level, you can
integrate up to 4 weapons into your body at a time.

##### Combat Augments

Also at 1st level, your combat augments allow you to use your integrated weapons to
overwhelm opponents with superior strength and speed. You gain the following benefits
while you are attacking with your integrated weapons:

```
⦁ You can use Dexterity instead of Strength for attack and damage rolls using
integrated weapons.
⦁ You can roll a d6 in place of the normal damage of your integrated weapon. This
damage increases as you level up, as shown in the Combat Augments Die column
in the Augmenticist table.
⦁ When you use the Attack action with an integrated weapon on your turn, you
can make an additional attack with a different integrated weapon as a bonus
action.
```

You can’t wear a shield and gain the benefits of this feature due to the clunky nature of
shields.

##### Overdrive

Starting at 2nd level, you can push your cybernetics beyond their usual limits, a process
known as overdrive. Your ability to push your body beyond its normal limits is
represented by your overdrive points, as shown in the Overdrive Points column of the
Augmenticist table.

You start with three overdrive features: targeted strikes, automatic defenses, and turbo
sprint. You learn more overdrive features as you gain levels in this class.

You regain all of your overdrive points when you complete a short or long rest, which
allows your internal systems to cool down and repair themselves.

Some of your overdrive features require your target to make a saving throw to resist the
feature's Effects. The saving throw DC is calculated as follows:

```
Overdrive save DC = 8 + your Proficiency Bonus + your Constitution modifier
```
**_Targeted Strikes_**

Immediately after you take the Attack action and attack with an integrated weapon on
your turn, you can spend 1 overdrive point to make two attacks with a different
integrated weapon.

**_Automatic Defenses_**

You can spend 1 overdrive point to take the Dodge action as a bonus action on your
turn.

**_Turbo Sprint_**

You can spend 1 overdrive point to take the Disengage or Dash action as a bonus action
on your turn, and your jump distance is doubled for the turn.

##### Upgraded Movement

Starting at 2nd level, your speed increases by 10 feet. This bonus increases when you
reach certain augmenticist levels, as shown in the augmenticist table.

At 9th level, your auto-stabilizing cogitators allow you to move along vertical surfaces
and across liquids on your turn without falling during the move.


##### Cybernetic Implants

When you reach 3rd level, you implant yourself with specific cybernetics to augment
your abilities. Your implants grant you features at 3rd level and again at 6th, 11th, and
17th level.

##### Deflect Missiles

Starting at 3rd level, your cybernetics allow you to repel kinetic and energy-based
attacks. You can use your reaction to deflect the attack when you are hit by a ranged
weapon attack. When you do so, the damage you take from the attack is reduced by
1d10 + your Constitution modifier + your augmenticist level.

If you reduce the damage to 0, you can reflect the attack. If you reflect an attack in this
way, you can spend 1 overdrive point to make a ranged Attack (range 20 feet/60 feet)
with the weapon or piece of ammunition you just reflected, as part of the same
reaction. You make this attack with proficiency, regardless of your weapon proficiencies,
and can use your combat augments die for the damage.

##### Ability Score Improvement

When you reach 4th level, and again at 8th, 12th, 16th, and 19th level, you can increase
one ability score of your choice by 2, or you can increase two ability scores of your
choice by 1. As normal, you can’t increase an ability score above 20 using this feature.

##### Hydraulics

Beginning at 4th level, you can use your reaction to reduce any falling damage you take
by an amount equal to five times your augmenticist level.

Additionally, you can use your Dexterity score instead of your Strength score to
determine your jumping heights and distances.

##### Extra Attack

Beginning at 5th level, you can attack twice, instead of once, whenever you take the
attack action on your turn.

##### Stunning Strike

Starting at 5th level, your blows can devastate even the strongest of foes. When you hit
a creature with an integrated weapon attack, you can expend 1 overdrive point to
attempt a stunning strike. The target must succeed on a Constitution saving throw or be


stunned until the end of your next turn. Once a creature succeeds on a saving throw
against this feature, it is immune to this feature until the start of your next turn.

##### Enhanced Strikes

Starting at 6th level, your integrated weapons count as enhanced for the purpose of
overcoming resistance and immunity to nonenhanced attacks and damage.

##### Autonomy of Mind

Starting at 7th level, you can use a bonus action to end one effect on yourself that is
causing you to be charmed or frightened.

##### Evasion

At 7th level, your instinctive agility lets you dodge out of the way of certain area effects,
such as a dreadnought’s _barrage_ or a _fireball_ power. When you are subjected to an
effect that allows you to make a Dexterity saving throw to take only half damage, you
instead take no damage if you succeed on the saving throw, and only half damage if you
fail.

##### Cybernetic Body

At 10th level, your heavily augmented body has made you immune to poisons and
nonenhanced diseases.

##### Omni-Lingual

Starting at 13th level, your integrated systems can identify and translate any spoken
language. Moreover, your integrated translators allow any creature that can understand
a language to understand what you say, as long as they speak at least one language.

##### Enhanced Core

Beginning at 14th level, your advanced augments grant you proficiency in all saving
throws.

Additionally, whenever you make a saving throw and fail, you can spend 1 overdrive
point to reroll it and take the second result.

##### Mechanized Immortality

At 15th level, your mechanical body sustains you so that you suffer none of the frailty of
old age, and you can't be aged through enhanced means. You can no longer die of old
age, and you no longer need food or water.


Additionally, you can use an action to remove 1 level of exhaustion from yourself.

##### Integrated Cloaking

Beginning at 18th level, you can use your bonus action to spend 4 overdrive points to
activate a cloaking field, becoming invisible for 1 minute. During that time, you also have
resistance to all damage but psionic damage.

##### Perfected Augments

At 20th level, your Strength, Dexterity, and Constitution scores increase by 2.
Additionally, when you score a critical hit, you regain 4 overdrive points.

#### Cybernetic Implants

Cybernetic implants are common throughout the galaxy, but only a select few dedicate
themselves to fully submerging themselves within the technology, and unlocking its
most intimate powers.

Most groups focus on one identity, such as the underhanded fighting utilized by hive
gangers, or the rigid military doctrine used in armies. All augmenticists rely on the same
basic cybernetics, only unlocking its true potential as they grow in power and
attunement to their technology. As such, an augmenticist needs to choose their
specialized cybernetic implants upon reaching 3rd level.

#### Combat Chem Implants

Combat chem implants are utilized for those who use drugs and stimulants to give them
the edge they need in combat.

##### Bonus Proficiencies

Your study of drugs gives you proficiency with alchemist’s supplies and the poisoner’s
kit.

##### Stim Injector

Starting when you choose these implants at 3rd level, you can inject stimulants into
your body, nullifying your pain. When you spend 1 or more overdrive points, such as on
targeted strikes, you gain an amount of temporary hit points equal to your Constitution
modifier (to a minimum of 1).


##### Focus Enhancer

Starting at 6th level, at the start of your turn, you can overflow your body with drugs to
increase your focus and precision (no action required). Until the start of your next turn,
you have advantage on all attack rolls, saving throws, and ability checks. Once you use
this feature, you can’t use it again until you complete a short or long rest, or until you
use 3 overdrive points to use it again.

##### Adrenaline Reserve

Beginning at 11th level, you have a special pump dedicated to flood you with
adrenaline. When you are reduced to 0 hit points, you can spend 1 overdrive point (no
action required) to have 1 hit point instead.

##### Toxin Valves

Starting at 17th level, you can use a bonus action and spend 1 to 10 overdrive points to
coat your weapon in a deadly toxin. The toxin lasts for 1 minute, or until you strike a
creature and deal damage to it, consuming the toxin.

When you deal damage to a creature, it must make a Constitution saving throw, and it
takes 2d10 necrotic damage per overdrive point spent on a failed save, or half as much
damage on a successful one.

#### Medicae Implants

Your implants are dedicated to healing, surgery, and sometimes murder.

##### Surgical Implements

Starting at 3rd level, you gain proficiency in the Medicine skill. Additionally, you have
proficiency in chirurgeon’s tools, and you can add double your proficiency bonus when
making checks with these tools.

Additionally, you have a built-in trauma kit with unlimited uses, and you can use a bonus
action to stabilize creatures within 5 feet of you.

##### Healing Mechadendrite

Also at 3rd level, you gain a cybernetic arm that extends from your back, known as a
mechadendrite. This mechadendrite comes equipped with chirurgeon’s tools. This arm
can’t be used to grasp objects that weigh more than 10 pounds, and it can't effectively
use weapons or a shield.


As an action, you can spend 1 overdrive point to surgerize a creature within 5 feet,
restoring a number of hit points equal to a roll of your Combat Augments die + your
Constitution modifier.

When you use your targeted strikes, you can replace one of the attacks with a use of
this feature without spending an overdrive point for the healing.

##### Medicine Chute

Starting at 6th level, your mechadendrite carries a slew of medicine with you. When you
use Healing Mechadendrite on a creature, you can also end one nonenhanced disease
or one of the following conditions affecting the creature: blinded, deafened, paralyzed,
poisoned, or stunned.

##### Combat Stimulants

Starting at 11th level, when you use targeted strikes, you can replace each of the attacks
with a use of your Healing Mechadendrite, without spending overdrive points for
healing.

Additionally, after healing a creature with your Healing Mechadendrite, you can inject a
healthy dose of combat stimulants (no action required), giving the creature advantage
on any attack rolls it makes before the end of their next turn.

##### Superior Chirurgeon

Starting at 17th level, you can cast the _cybernetic resurrection_ tech power using this
feature. When resurrecting a creature this way, you can keep the creature the original
race it originally was, instead of turning them into a techfused. Once you cast this
power, you can’t do so again for 10 days.

Additionally, you can target up to 6 creatures within 30 feet of you to improve their
health. For 8 hours, you increase their maximum hit points and current hit points by an
amount equal to half your level. Once you use this feature, you can’t use it again until
you complete a long rest.

## Berserker

A tall human tribesman strides through blizzards, draped in fur and hefting his axe. He
laughs as he charges towards the group of orks that dared to attack his feral world’s


villages.
An ogryn snarls at the latest challenger to his authority, ready to break his
opponent’s neck with his bare hands, as he did the last six opponents.
Frothing from the mouth, a Blood Angel slams his gauntlet into the face of his dark
eldar foe, then turns to drive his armored elbow into the gut of another, splintering ribs
and fracturing bones.
These berserkers, different as they might be, are defined by an uncanny rage they
enter when the dawn of battle rises. More than a mere emotion, their anger and
ferocity is that of a cornered animal, yet their purpose is as clear as the eye of a storm.
For some, their rage springs from the communion of technology and flesh, using
cybernetics to quell any unnecessary emotions to fuel their fury in battle. For others,
this rage is forged from years of battle, discipline, and dedication to their cause.

#### Quick Build

You can make a berserker quickly by following these suggestions. First, make Strength
your highest ability modifier. Your next highest score should be Constitution and
Dexterity. Second, choose the mercenary background.

#### Class Features

As a berserker, you gain the following class features:

##### Hit Points

**Hit Dice** : 1d12 per berserker level
**Hit Points at 1st Level** : 12 + your Constitution modifier
**Hit Points at Higher Levels** : 1d12 (or 7) + your Constitution modifier per berserker level
after 1st

**Proficiencies
Armor** : Light armor, medium armor, shields
**Weapons** : Simple weapons, martial weapons
**Tools** : none
**Saving Throws** : Strength, Constitution
**Skills** : Choose two from Acrobatics, Athletics, Insight, Intimidation, Lore, Medicine,
Nature, Perception, and Survival.

**Equipment**
You start with the following equipment, in addition to the equipment granted by your
background:


```
⦁ (a) a greataxe or (b) any martial melee weapon
⦁ (a) two handaxes or (b) any simple weapon or (c) a shield
⦁ (a) scale mail or (b) mesh armor
⦁ An explorer’s pack and five javelins
```
##### The Berserker

```
Level Proficiency
Bonus
```
```
Features Rage Rage Dam
```
```
1st +2 Unarmored Defense, Rage 2 +2
2nd +2 Reckless Attack, Danger Sense 2 +2
3rd +2 War Path 3 +2
4th +2 Ability Score Improvement 3 +2
5th +3 Extra Attack, Fast Movement 3 +2
6th +3 Path feature 4 +2
7th +3 Feral Instinct 4 +2
8th +3 Ability Score Improvement 4 +2
9th +4 Brutal Critical (1 die) 4 +3
10th +4 War Path feature 4 +3
11th +4 Relentless Rage 4 +3
12th +4 Ability Score Improvement 5 +3
13th +5 Brutal Critical (2 die) 5 +3
14th +5 War Path feature 5 +3
15th +5 Persistent Rage 5 +3
16th +5 Ability Score Improvement 5 +4
17th +6 Brutal Critical (3 die) 6 +4
18th +6 Indomitable Might 6 +4
19th +6 Ability Score Improvement 6 +4
20th +6 Champion of War Unlimited +4
```
##### Unarmored Defense

While you are not wearing any armor, your armor class equals 10 + your Dexterity
modifier + your Constitution modifier. You can use a shield and still gain this benefit.

##### Rage

In battle, you fight with a primal fury. On your turn, you can enter a rage as a bonus
action.

While in a rage, you gain the following benefits if you aren't wearing heavy armor:


```
⦁ You have advantage on Strength checks and Strength saving throws.
⦁ When you make a melee weapon attack using Strength, you gain a +2 bonus to
the damage roll. This bonus increases as you level.
⦁ You have resistance to energy and kinetic damage.
```
If you are able to cast powers, you can't cast them or concentrate on them while in a
rage.

Your rage lasts for 1 minute. It ends early if you are knocked unconscious or if your turn
ends and you haven't attacked a hostile creature since your last turn or taken damage
since then. You can also end your rage on your turn as a bonus action.

Once you have entered a rage the maximum number of times for your berserker level,
you must finish a long rest before you can enter a rage again. You may use rage 2 times
at 1st level, 3 at 3rd, 4 at 6th, 5 at 12th, and 6 at 17th.

##### Danger Sense

At 2nd level, you gain an uncanny sense of when things nearby aren't as they should be,
giving you an edge when you dodge away from danger. You have advantage on
Dexterity saving throws against effects that you can see, such as traps and powers. To
gain this benefit, you can't be blinded, deafened, or incapacitated.

##### Reckless Attack

Starting at 2nd level, you can throw aside all concern for defense to attack with fierce
desperation. When you make your first attack on your turn, you can decide to attack
recklessly. Doing so gives you advantage on melee weapon attack rolls using strength
during this turn, but attack rolls against you have advantage until your next turn.

##### War Path

At 3rd level, you choose a path that shapes the nature of your rage, such as the Path of
Hatred. Your choice grants you features at 3rd level and again at 6th, 10th, and 14th
levels.

##### Ability Score Improvement

When you reach 4th level, and again at 8th, 12th, 16th, and 19th level, you can increase
one ability score of your choice by 2, or you can increase two ability scores of your
choice by 1. As normal, you can’t increase an ability score above 20 using this feature.


##### Extra Attack

Beginning at 5th level, you can attack twice, instead of once, whenever you take the
Attack action on your turn.

##### Fast Movement

Starting at 5th level, your walking speed increases by 10 feet while you aren’t wearing
heavy armor.

##### Battle Instinct

By 7th level, your instincts are so honed that you have advantage on initiative rolls.

Additionally, if you are surprised at the beginning of combat and aren't incapacitated,
you can act normally on your first turn, but only if you enter your rage before doing
anything else on that turn.

##### Brutal Critical

Beginning at 9th level, you can roll one additional weapon damage die when
determining the extra damage for a critical hit with a melee attack.

This increases to two additional dice at 13th level and three additional dice at 17th level.

##### Relentless Rage

Starting at 11th level, your rage can keep you fighting despite grievous wounds. If you
drop to 0 hit points while you're in a rage and don't die outright, you can make a DC 10
Constitution saving throw. If you succeed, you drop to 1 hit point instead.

Each time you use this feature after the first, the DC increases by 5. When you finish a
short or long rest, the DC resets to 10.

##### Persistent Rage

Beginning at 15th level, your rage is so fierce that it ends early only if you fall
unconscious or if you choose to end it.

##### Indomitable Might

Beginning at 18th level, if your total for a Strength check is less than your Strength
score, you can use that score in place of the total.


##### Champion of War

At 20th level, you embody the power of war. Your Strength and Constitution scores
increase by 4. Your maximum for those scores is now 26.

#### War Paths

#### Path of Hatred

The sharpest blade is dull compared to the purest hatred. Along this path, many have
fallen prey to the mindless rages that suits a life of war and conquest.

##### Unending Fury

Starting when you choose this path at 3rd level, you can channel your hatred into your
weapon strikes. While you're raging, the first creature you hit on each of your turns with
a weapon attack takes extra damage equal to 1d6 + half your berserker level. The extra
damage deals the same damage type as your weapon.

##### Rampager’s Dash

Also at 3rd level, when you reduce a creature to 0 hit points on your turn, you can use a
bonus action to immediately move up to half your speed.

##### Mindless Rage

Beginning at 6th level, you can't be charmed or frightened while raging. If you are
charmed or frightened when you enter your rage, the effect is suspended for the
duration of the rage.

##### Furious Charge

Beginning at 10th level, you can take the Dash action as a bonus action while you are
raging.

##### Retaliation

Starting at 14th level, when you take damage from a creature that is within 5 feet of
you, you can use your reaction to make a melee weapon attack against that creature.

#### Path of Augmentation


In order to become more powerful, you rely on the cybernetics that empower your
body. The flesh is weak, and you have used metal to overcome its weaknesses.

##### Utility Cybernetics

When you choose this path at 3rd level, you learn the tech powers _mending_ and
_analyze,_ and you can cast them without expending tech points. You can cast _analyze_ this
way a number of times equal to your Constitution modifier (minimum of one). You
regain all expended uses when you complete a long rest.

##### Dermal Armor

Also at 3rd level, you gain dermal armor that can harden under extreme stress, causing
your skin to have a metallic appearance. While you are raging, you have resistance to all
damage except psionic damage.

##### Support Cybernetics

At 6th level you gain a mechanical exoskeleton to further strengthen your body. Your
carrying capacity (including maximum load and maximum lift) is doubled and you have
advantage on Strength checks made to push, pull, lift, or break objects.

Additionally, you can choose one of the following cybernetics below, and gain the
benefits of it:

```
⦁ Adaptable Hand Mesh. You gain a climbing and swimming speed equal to your
walking speed.
⦁ Holdout Cavity. You have a holdout cavity placed in one location on your body of
your choice, such as your arm or leg. This holdout cavity is a small compartment
inside of your body that can fully conceal items placed inside of it. A holdout
cavity can be used to store and hide a light weapon or item of similar size. It
takes an action to store or withdraw an item or weapon from your holdout
cavity.
⦁ Panspectral Optics. You can see up to 1 mile away with no difficulty, able to
discern even fine details as though looking at something no more than 100 feet
away from you. Additionally, dim light doesn't impose disadvantage on your
Wisdom (Perception) checks.
```
##### More Machine than Man

Starting at 10th level, your cybernetics allow you to become immune to poison and
nonenhanced disease. Additionally, you ignore nonenhanced difficult terrain.


##### Hydraulic Override

At 14th level, you gain the ability to thrust people into a prone position. While you're in
a rage, you can use a bonus action on your turn to knock a size Large or smaller creature
prone when you hit it with melee weapon attack.

## Courser

Exhausted but determined, a human stalks the alleyways of the hive city, hunting the
quarry he knows is behind the murders in the habblock. Clutching a pistol in both hands,
he steps into the alleyway full of mutants and gangers. Spinning around, he becomes a
hurricane of bullets, felling each enemy one after another.
After tumbling away from a shell’s explosion, a mutant finds her footing, only to fire
off two shots from her carbine at the oncoming horde of tyranids. Shrugging off the
waves of fear that dare to overturn the tumultuous tides of her mind, she steels herself,
releasing a cluster of grenades she had prepared, watching as the overgrown bugs turn
into crisp husks.
Glancing at his dataslate, a techfused looks through the eyes of his servo skull,
tracing the movements of a shadow from amongst the rooftops. He readies his sniper
shot, his artificial lungs not making the slightest of noise as he lines his shot.
Coursers are the first on the scene of the crime, and the last one to see their target.
Regardless of terrain, distance, or obstacles, a courser is most suited to tracking and
hunting, using tech powers and weaponry to overcome their endeavors.

#### Quick Build

You can make a courser quickly by following these suggestions. First, make Strength or
Dexterity your highest ability modifier, depending on whether you want to focus on
melee combat or on ranged weapons (or finesse weapons). Your next highest score
should be Intelligence. Second, choose the mercenary background.

#### Class Features

As a courser, you have the following class features.

##### Hit Points

**Hit Dice** : 1d10 per courser level
**Hit Points at 1st Level** : 10 + your Constitution modifier
**Hit Points at Higher Levels** : 1d10 (or 6) + your Constitution modifier per courser level


after 1st

**Starting Proficiencies
Armor** : Light armor, medium armor, and shields
**Weapons** : Simple weapons, martial weapons
**Tools** : None
**Saving Throws** : Strength, Dexterity
**Skills** : Choose three from Athletics, Acrobatics, Insight, Investigation, Lore, Nature,
Occult, Perception, Piloting, Stealth, Survival, and Tech.

**Equipment**
You start with the following equipment, in addition to the equipment granted by your
background
⦁ (a) trooper armor or (b) mesh armor
⦁ (a) two shortswords or (b) a martial melee weapon and a shield
⦁ (a) assault rifle and two magazines or (b) lasgun and two power cells
⦁ An explorer’s pack and two daggers

##### The Courser

```
Level Proficiency
Bonus
```
```
Features Target Lock Tech Powers
Known
```
```
Te
```
```
1st +2 Courser Training, Target Lock 2 —
2nd +2 Fighting Style, Techcasting 2 7
3rd +2 Courser Technique 2 9

7th +3 Technique feature 3 14

```

```

20th +6 Master Courser 6 30
```
##### Courser Training

Beginning at 1st level, you are difficult to pin down during a fight. You can move up to
half your speed as a reaction when an enemy ends its turn within 5 feet of you. This
movement doesn’t provoke opportunity attacks.

Additionally, choose one of the skills you are proficient in. You can add double your
proficiency bonus to checks made with that skill.

##### Target Lock

At 1st level, your unique technology allows you to track enemies and land hits with
deadly precision. As a bonus action, you can activate your target lock and gain the
following benefits:

```
⦁ Your weapon attacks deal an extra 1d6 damage of the same type as your
weapon.
⦁ You have advantage on Perception checks made to detect creatures.
⦁ Your attacks ignore half and three-quarters cover.
```
Your target lock lasts for 1 minute. It ends early if you are incapacitated, or if you end it
early as a bonus action.

You can use this feature twice, and you can use it more often at higher levels, as shown
in the Target Lock column of the Courser table. You regain all expended uses when you
finish a long rest.

At 9th level, this damage increases to 1d8, and you can see invisible creatures within 30
feet of you while this feature is activated. At 17th level, the damage increases to 1d10,
and you can see through illusions, shapechangers, and into the immaterium to a range
of 30 feet while this feature is activated.

##### Fighting Style

Beginning at 2nd level, you adopt a particular style of fighting as your specialty. Choose
one of the Fighting Style options, listed below. You can’t take a Fighting Style option
more than once, even if you later get to choose again.

```
Blind Fighting. You have blindsight with a range of 10 feet. Within that range, you
```

can effectively see anything that isn't behind total cover, even if you're blinded or in
darkness. Moreover, you can see an invisible creature within that range, unless the
creature successfully hides from you.
**_Defense._** While you are wearing armor, you gain a +1 bonus to AC.
**_Dueling._** When you are wielding a weapon in one hand and no other weapons, you
gain a +2 bonus to damage rolls with that weapon.
**_Great Weapon Fighting._** When you roll a 1 or 2 on a damage die for an attack you
make with a weapon that you are wielding with two hands, you can reroll the die and
must use the new roll, even if the new roll is a 1 or a 2. The weapon must have the two-
handed or versatile property for you to gain this benefit.
**_Interception._** When a creature you can see hits a target, other than you, within 5
feet of you with an attack, you can use your reaction to reduce the damage the target
takes by 1d10 + your proficiency bonus (to a minimum of 0 damage). You must be
wielding a shield or a simple or martial weapon to use this reaction.
**_Thrown Weapon Fighting._** You can draw a weapon that has the thrown property as
part of the attack you make with the weapon. In addition, when you hit with a ranged
attack using a thrown weapon, you gain a +2 bonus to the damage roll.
**_Two-Weapon Fighting._** When you engage in two-weapon fighting, you can add your
ability modifier to the damage of the second attack. Furthermore, being within 5 feet of
a hostile creature doesn’t impose disadvantage on your ranged attack rolls with one-
handed weapons.
**_Unarmed Fighting._** Your unarmed strikes can deal bludgeoning damage equal to 1d6
+ your Strength modifier on a hit. If you aren’t wielding any weapons or a shield when
you make the attack roll, the d6 becomes a d8. At the start of each of your turns, you
can deal 1d4 bludgeoning damage to one creature grappled by you.

##### Techcasting

By the time you reach 2nd level, you have learned to use technology to cast tech
powers, like a savant does.

**_Tech Powers Known_**

You learn 7 tech powers of your choice, and you learn more at higher levels, as shown in
the Tech Powers Known column of the Courser table. You may not learn a tech power of
a level higher than your Max Power Level.

**_Tech Points_**

You have a number of tech points equal to your courser level x 2, as shown in the Tech
Points column of the Courser table. When you cast a power, you expend a number of
tech points equal to 1 + the power’s level. You regain all expended tech points when you
finish a long rest.


**_Max Power Level_**

Many tech powers can be overpowered, consuming more tech points to create a
greater effect. You can overpower these abilities to a maximum level, which increases at
higher levels, as shown in the Max Power Level column of the Courser table.

You may only cast tech powers at 6th, 7th, 8th, and 9th-level once. You regain the ability
to do so after a long rest.

**_Techcasting Ability_**

Your techcasting ability is the ability score you use to cast tech powers. Your techcasting
ability is Intelligence. You use this ability score modifier whenever a power refers to
your techcasting ability. Additionally, you use this ability score modifier when setting the
saving throw DC for a tech power you cast and when making an attack roll with one.

```
Tech save DC = 8 + your proficiency bonus + your techcasting modifier
Tech attack modifier = your proficiency bonus + your techcasting modifier
```
##### Courser Technique

Also at 3rd level, you choose to focus on a specific courser technique, which is detailed
at the end of the class description. Your choice grants you features at 3rd level and
again at 7th, 11th, and 15th level.

##### Ability Score Improvement

When you reach 4th level, and again at 8th, 12th, 16th, and 19th level, you can increase
one ability score of your choice by 2, or you can increase two ability scores of your
choice by 1. As normal, you can’t increase an ability score above 20 using this feature.

##### Extra Attack

Beginning at 5th level, you can attack twice, instead of once, whenever you take the
Attack action on your turn.

##### Wanderer’s Movement

At 6th level, your walking speed increases by 10, and you gain a climbing speed and a
swimming speed equal to your walking speed.

##### Tireless Pursuit

At 10th level, when you activate your target lock, you also gain an amount of temporary


hit points equal to your courser level.

Additionally, when you roll for a Survival check, if the result on the d20 is below your
courser level, you can treat the roll as being equal to your courser level instead. For
example, if a 13th-level courser rolls a 12 or lower on a Survival check, the courser can
treat that roll as a 13, and then add any additional modifiers on top of that.

##### Combat Cloak

At 14th level, you can choose to go invisible when you activate target lock. This
invisibility lasts until your target lock ends. Once you use this feature, you can’t use it
again until you complete a short or long rest.

##### Perfect Lock

At 18th level, your target lock damage die deals maximum damage, instead of rolling for
the amount.

##### Master Courser

At 20th level, you become an unparalleled hunter. Once on each of your turns, you can
add your Intelligence modifier to the attack and damage roll of an attack you make.

#### Courser Techniques

#### Hunter Technique

The hunter technique is utilized by coursers that desire to know the weaknesses of their
prey, while also being able to defend against their prey’s attacks, or to slay their minions
quickly.

##### Hunter’s Insight

When you choose this technique at 3rd level, when you attack and deal damage to a
creature while your target lock is active, you can learn if the creature has any damage
immunities, resistances, or vulnerabilities, and you learn what they are.

##### Pinpoint Weakness

Also starting at 3rd level, if an allied creature is within 5 feet of a hostile creature and
isn’t incapacitated, you have advantage on the first attack roll you make on your turn
against the hostile creature.


##### Reflexive Defense

Starting at 7th level, when you are hit by an attack or fail a saving throw, but before any
effects take place, you can use your reaction to gain a bonus to your AC or the saving
throw equal to your proficiency bonus, potentially causing the attack to miss or the
saving throw to succeed.

##### Cleave the Tide

Starting at 11th level, you have learned to cleave the tide of enemies that stand against
you. You can use your action to make melee attacks against any number of creatures
within 5 feet of you, with a separate attack roll for each target.

Alternatively, you can use your action to make a ranged attack against any number of
creatures in a 10-foot square within your weapon’s range. You must make a separate
attack roll for each target.

##### Evasion

At 15th level, when you are subjected to an effect, such as a psyker’s _ice storm_ or a
savant’s _fireball_ , that allows you to make a Dexterity saving throw to take only half
damage, you instead take no damage if you succeed on a saving throw, and only half
damage if you fail.

#### Stalker Technique

The stalker technique focuses on stealth and exploiting the weaknesses of their prey,
until they finally find the moment to bring them down.

##### Ambush Augments

At 3rd level, you can take the Hide action as part of the bonus action you use to activate
your target lock. While target lock is active, you can take the Hide action as a bonus
action on each of your turns.

##### Precision Strike

Also starting at 3rd level, when you deal damage to a creature with a weapon attack,
you can make a precision strike against the target. The creature suffers one of the
following effects:

```
⦁ Until the start of your next turn, the creature’s movement is 0.
```

```
⦁ You can cause the next attack roll the creature makes within 1 minute to be at
disadvantage.
⦁ You can cause the creature to have disadvantage on the next Strength, Dexterity,
or Constitution saving throw it makes within 1 minute.
```
You have a number of precision strikes equal to double your proficiency bonus, and you
regain all uses at the end of a long rest.

##### Quick Pounce

At 7th level, while your target lock is activated, you can take the Dash action as a bonus
action on your turn. If you dash in this way, you do not provoke opportunity attacks until
the beginning of your next turn.

##### Predict Assault

At 11th level, when you are attacked, you can roll the damage die of your target lock
and reduce the attack roll by that amount. You can use this feature once per turn.

##### Critical Targeting

At 15th level, while your target lock is active, your weapon attacks deal critical strikes on
a roll of 19 or 20.

## Crusader

Amongst the warring armies, a few voices are heard above the shelling artillery and
exploding bolt rounds. These voices ring true, inspiring the people around them,
uplifting even the common man to a warrior of vengeance to strike down the enemies
that surround them. Crusaders inspire those around them to perform courageous acts,
bolster themselves against oncoming hordes of foes, and deliver righteous retribution
upon those who dare to put themselves in opposition to their cause. In times of dire
need, a crusader may even implore their god or deity for aid, sending down an angel or
daemon of great power to serve them, or manifesting a miracle into existence.

#### Quick Build

You can make a crusader quickly by following these suggestions. First, make Strength or
Dexterity your highest ability modifier, depending if you want to focus on melee or
ranged combat (or finesse weapons). Your next highest score should be Constitution.
Second, choose the acolyte background.


#### Class Features

As a crusader, you gain the following class features.

##### Hit Points

**Hit Dice** : 1d10 per crusader level
**Hit Points at 1st Level** : 10 + your Constitution modifier
**Hit Points at Higher Levels** : 1d10 (or 6) + your Constitution modifier per crusader level
after 1st

**Starting Proficiencies**
You are proficient with the following items, in addition to any proficiencies provided by
your race or background.

**Armor** : Light armor, medium armor, heavy armor, shields
**Weapons** : Simple weapons, martial weapons
**Tools** : None
**Saving Throws** : Strength, Constitution
**Skills** : Choose three from Athletics, Acrobatics, Insight, Intimidation, Lore, Occult,
Performance, Persuasion, Piloting, Tech, and Survival.

**Starting Equipment**
You start with the following items, plus anything provided by your background.

```
⦁ (a) battle armor or (b) mesh armor, assault rifle, and 2 magazines
⦁ (a) a martial weapon and a shield or (b) two martial weapons
⦁ (a) a las carbine and 2 power cells or (b) two handaxes
⦁ (a) a dungeoneer's pack or (b) an explorer's pack
```
##### The Crusader

```
Level Proficiency
Bonus
```
```
Features Valo
```
```
1st +2 Fighting Style, Vengeful Strike
2nd +2 Faithful Rest, Valor
3rd +2 Crusader Oath
4th +2 Ability Score Increase
5th +3 Extra Attack, Valor (d8)
6th +3 Battle Cry
```

```
7th +3 Crusader Oath Feature

15th +5 Valor (d12)
16th +5 Ability Score Increase
17th +6 Last Stand (three uses), Closed Mind
18th +6 Duty Unto Death
19th +6 Ability Score Increase
20th +6 Divine Intervention Improvement
```
##### Fighting Style

You adopt a particular style of fighting as your specialty. Choose a Fighting Style from
the list of optional features. You can't take the same Fighting Style option more than
once, even if you get to choose again.

**_Blind Fighting._** You have blindsight with a range of 10 feet. Within that range, you
can effectively see anything that isn't behind total cover, even if you're blinded or in
darkness. Moreover, you can see an invisible creature within that range, unless the
creature successfully hides from you.
**_Defense._** While you are wearing armor, you gain a +1 bonus to AC.
**_Dueling._** When you are wielding a weapon in one hand and no other weapons, you
gain a +2 bonus to damage rolls with that weapon.
**_Great Weapon Fighting._** When you roll a 1 or 2 on a damage die for an attack you
make with a weapon that you are wielding with two hands, you can reroll the die and
must use the new roll, even if the new roll is a 1 or a 2. The weapon must have the two-
handed or versatile property for you to gain this benefit.
**_Interception._** When a creature you can see hits a target, other than you, within 5
feet of you with an attack, you can use your reaction to reduce the damage the target
takes by 1d10 + your proficiency bonus (to a minimum of 0 damage). You must be
wielding a shield or a simple or martial weapon to use this reaction.
**_Thrown Weapon Fighting._** You can draw a weapon that has the thrown property as
part of the attack you make with the weapon. In addition, when you hit with a ranged
attack using a thrown weapon, you gain a +2 bonus to the damage roll.
**_Two-Weapon Fighting._** When you engage in two-weapon fighting, you can add your
ability modifier to the damage of the second attack. Furthermore, being within 5 feet of


a hostile creature doesn’t impose disadvantage on your ranged attack rolls with one-
handed weapons.
**_Unarmed Fighting._** Your unarmed strikes can deal bludgeoning damage equal to 1d6
+ your Strength modifier on a hit. If you aren’t wielding any weapons or a shield when
you make the attack roll, the d6 becomes a d8. At the start of each of your turns, you
can deal 1d4 bludgeoning damage to one creature grappled by you.

##### Vengeful Strike

You can make allies strike, even when it is not their turn. As a bonus action, you can
allow an allied creature within 60 feet of you that can hear you to make one weapon
attack using their reaction.

You can use this feature a number of times equal to your proficiency bonus, and you
regain all expended uses at the end of a short or long rest.

##### Valor

Beginning at 2nd level, you can inspire others through stirring words or rallying cries.
Your valor is represented by a number of valor points. Your crusader level determines
the number of points you have, as shown in the Valor Points column of the Crusader
table.

You can spend these points to use certain features. When you make an attack against a
hostile creature or when you use your vengeful strike feature, you can spend a valor
point and roll a valor die, a d6, to achieve one of the following effects:

```
⦁ One creature within 60 feet of you gains hit points equal to one roll of your valor
die.
⦁ When you or an allied creature deal damage with a weapon attack, you can
cause the attack to deal additional damage equal to one roll of your valor die.
⦁ You or an allied creature within 60 feet of you gain a bonus to their AC against
the next attack that targets them equal to one roll of the valor die. This bonus to
AC lasts until the start of your next turn.
```
You regain any expended uses of valor when you finish a short or long rest.

Your Valor die changes when you reach certain levels in this class. The die becomes a d8
at 5th level, a d10 at 10th level, and a d12 at 15th level.

##### Faithful Rest


At 2nd level, you can use oration to help your allies recover during a short rest. If you or
any friendly creatures who can hear your performance spend one or more Hit Dice to
regain hit points at the end of a short rest, each of those creatures regains an extra
amount of hit points equal to one roll of your valor die.

##### Crusader Oath

Starting at 3rd level, you take the crusader oath that binds you to service. This oath is
something that each crusader takes personally, sometimes in front of a cleric or
professor of their faith, and personally interprets based on their own beliefs, ethics, and
experiences. You gain features for this oath at 3rd, 7th, and 14th level.

##### Ability Score Improvement

When you reach 4th level, and again at 8th, 12th, 16th, and 19th level, you can increase
one ability score of your choice by 2, or you can increase two ability scores of your
choice by 1. As normal, you can’t increase an ability score above 20 using this feature.

##### Extra Attack

Beginning at 5th level, you can attack twice, instead of once, whenever you take the
Attack action on your turn.

##### Battle Cry

At 6th level, you gain the ability to shrug off mind-influencing effects for yourself and
your teammates. As a bonus action, you can start a chant, mantra, or speech that lasts
for 1 minute. During that time, you and any friendly creatures within 60 feet of you have
advantage on saving throws against being frightened and charmed. A creature must be
able to hear you to gain this benefit. The performance ends early if you are
incapacitated or silenced or if you voluntarily end it (no action required).

Once you use this feature, you can’t use it again until you finish a short or long rest.

At 11th level, you and any friendly creatures within 60 feet of you have immunity to
being frightened and charmed when you use this feature..

##### Last Stand

Beginning at 9th level, your resolve causes you and your allies to keep going. When you
or an allied creature within 60 feet of you that can see you is reduced to 0 hit points but
not killed outright, you can use your reaction to cause that creature to drop to 1 hit
point instead, and you can’t use this feature again until you finish a long rest.


You can use this feature twice between long rests starting at 13th level and three times
between long rests starting at 17th level.

##### Divine Intervention

Beginning at 10th level, you can call on a miracle to intervene on your behalf when your
need is great.

Imploring for a miracle requires your action. Describe the assistance you seek, and roll
percentile dice, a d100. If you roll a number equal to or lower than your crusader level,
your miracle manifests into reality. The DM chooses the nature of the intervention; the
effect of any psychic power would be appropriate, or the summoning of a daemon or
saint temporarily to fight alongside you. If your miracle manifests into reality, you can't
use this feature again for 7 days. Otherwise, you can use it again after you finish a long
rest.

At 20th level, your call for intervention succeeds automatically, no roll required.

##### Closed Mind

Starting at 17th level, your mind is set in its path to see through any deception. You
automatically succeed on saving throws against illusions, having your thoughts read, and
your mood altered. Additionally, you have immunity to psionic damage.

##### Duty Unto Death

At 18th level, you and allied creatures without 60 feet of you that can hear you are
always under the effects of your battle cry feature. This effect is suspended if you are
incapacitated or silenced.

Additionally, at the end of a long rest, you can choose up to ten creatures within 60 feet
of you that can hear you, and give them a rousing speech. Their maximum and current
hit points increase by an amount equal to your crusader level. This benefit lasts for 8
hours, or until you die.

#### Crusader Oaths

Each crusader takes an oath, and up until this point, they might have viewed their
journey up until this point merely training for what is to come. A crusader oath is what
binds them to service of their cause, but many crusaders have their own vision of what
their oath means, and what it means to break their oath. If an oath is broken, a crusader
may decide to take another oath, or to seek penitence or forgiveness by a priest or
professor of their faith or creed.


Your Crusader Oath gives you features at 3rd level, 7th level, and 14th level.

#### Oath of the Apostle

Apostles are holy men of their faith, and seek out to do righteousness for their just
cause. These apostles are often studious of their religious materials, and seek to instill
fanaticism and zealotry within the ranks of their allies. Although each oath differs in
severity and interpretation, the tenets an Oath of the Apostle might take look similar to
this:

**_Shepherd of the Flock._** As I was once a sheep, I am now a shepherd, and I herd my
followers into enlightenment.
**_Sacred Texts._** The sacred texts show us wisdom and truth. It is up to us to divine
their meaning.
**_War of the Word._** To win the hearts of the people, your words must show them the
truth.

##### War Scholar

Beginning at 3rd level when you choose this oath, you are well-learned in the art of war
and philosophy. Choose two of the following skills: Insight, Investigation, Lore, Nature,
and Occult. You gain proficiency in these skills, and you can add double your proficiency
bonus to skill checks made when using these skills.

##### Fanaticism

Starting at 3rd level, you can inspire allies to fight beyond their limit. When you use your
vengeful strike feature, the creature gains 5 temporary hit points. When it gains these
temporary hit points, it can immediately move up to half of its speed, without provoking
opportunity attacks, before or after taking its attack.

The number of temporary hit points increases when you reach certain levels in this
class, increasing to 8 at 5th level, 11 at 10th level, and 14 at 15th level.

##### Sacred Word

Starting at 7th level, you can treat any roll on the d20 of 9 or lower as a 10 when making
Intimidation, Persuasion and Performance checks.

##### Summon Champion of Faith

Starting at 14th level, you can use an action to summon an otherworldly champion of


your faith for 1 minute to an unoccupied spot within 30 feet of you. This champion uses
the statistics provided below, and obeys any verbal command you issue it. The
champion acts on your initiative. If you are incapacitated or did not issue it orders, the
champion will defend you and itself to the best of its ability.

Once you summon a champion of faith, you can’t do so again until you complete a long
rest.

### Champion of Faith

```
Medium daemon, any lawful alignment
Armor Class 15 + your proficiency bonus
Hit Points 50 + your level
Speed 30 ft., fly 40 ft.
```

```
Multiattack. The champion makes two attacks with its greatsword.
```
```
Flaming Greatsword. Melee Weapon Attack: 5 + your proficiency bonus to
hit, reach 5 ft., one target. Hit: (1d8 + 4 + your proficiency bonus) slashing
damage plus 7 (2d6) fire damage.
```
#### Oath of the Penitent

The penitent are those who have strayed from the path of righteousness, or have erred
in some way. Some penitent know that they can never return, and wish to live their lives
on the outskirts. Other penitent choose to instead look at this as climbing their way back
to holiness. Many who sear themselves to the Oath of the Penitent cast away their
armor and clothes, wearing only a thin cloth as punishment. Although each oath differs
in severity and interpretation, the tenets an Oath of the Penitent might take look similar
to this:

**_Let Not Weakness Define._** Weakness has led me to this path, but strength is my
absolution.
**_Redemption Requires Sacrifice._** If I am to redeem myself, I must be willing to
sacrifice everything.


**_Not All Who Wander Are Lost._** Although it is a winding road I wander, I am never
lost in my pursuit of redemption.

##### Unarmored Defense

Starting at 3rd level when you choose this oath, while you are not wearing armor, your
AC is 10 + your Dexterity modifier + your Constitution modifier.

##### Repentant Fervor

Also at 3rd level, whenever you spend one or more valor points, you have advantage on
the first weapon attack you make before the end of your next turn. Alternatively, you
can allow an allied creature to gain advantage on the next attack roll they make using
your vengeful strike feature.

##### Devastating Critical

At 7th level, when you score a critical hit with a weapon attack, you deal an additional
amount of damage equal to your level in this class.

##### Redeemer

Starting at 14th level, when you are below half of your maximum hit points, you have
resistance to energy and kinetic damage.

## Exorcist

Clad in heavy armor, a space marine sends out a sheet of warp flame, incinerating his
enemies. An eldar clashes against daemons, before sending them back screaming into
the warp. The inquisitor places his brand against the daemonhost’s back, screaming out
litanies of fury and the Emperor, coaxing the daemon out, its twisted body forcibly
pulled from the body of its vessel.
Exorcists are the frontline of defense between that which lies beyond the veil of
reality. Exorcists protect reality from these horrors, but can have very different ideals
and ways to accomplish this. Some exorcists might believe that a daemon must be
purged at all costs, and is willing to commit grand atrocities if it means destroying the
greater evil, while more radical exorcists might create pacts with daemons to gain their
powers, in order to banish even more from realspace.

#### Quick Build

You can make an exorcist quickly by following these suggestions. First, make Strength


your highest ability modifier. Your next highest score should be Charisma or
Constitution. Second, choose the witchhunter background.

#### Class Features

As an exorcist, you gain the following class features.

##### Hit Points

**Hit Dice** : 1d10 per exorcist level
**Hit Points at 1st Level** : 10 + your Constitution modifier
**Hit Points at Higher Levels** : 1d10 (or 6) + your Constitution modifier per exorcist level
after 1st

**Starting Proficiencies**
You are proficient with the following items, in addition to any proficiencies provided by
your race or background.

**Armor** : Light armor, medium armor, heavy armor, shields
**Weapons** : Simple weapons, martial weapons
**Tools** : Calligrapher’s tools
**Saving Throws** : Wisdom, Charisma
**Skills** : Choose two from Athletics, Insight, Intimidation, Medicine, Occult, Performance,
and Persuasion.

**Starting Equipment**
You start with the following items, plus anything provided by your background.

```
⦁ (a) a martial weapon and a shield or (b) two martial weapons
⦁ (a) five javelins or (b) a pistol with two magazines
⦁ (a) a priest's pack or (b) an explorer's pack
⦁ Battle armor and calligrapher’s tools
```
##### The Exorcist

```
17th +6 — 27 34 5th
18th +6 Aura Improvements 28 36 5th
19th +6 Ability Score Improvement 29 38 5th
20th +6 Exorcist Order feature 30 40 5th
```
##### Psycasting

You have channeled the ability to channel the immaterium to fuel your psychic powers.
See chapter 10 for the general rules of casting powers and chapter 11 for the psychic
powers list.

**_Psychic Powers Known_**

You learn 5 psychic powers of your choice, and you learn more at higher levels, as
shown in the Psychic Powers Known column of the Exorcist table. You may not learn a
psychic power of a level higher than your Max Power Level.

**_Psyker Points_**

You have a number of psyker points equal to your exorcist level x 2, as shown in the
Psyker Points column of the Exorcist table. When you cast a power, you expend a
number of psyker points equal to 1 + the power’s level. You regain all expended psyker
points when you finish a long rest.

**_Max Power Level_**

Many psychic powers can be overpowered, consuming more psyker points to create a
greater effect. You can overpower these abilities to a maximum level, which increases at
higher levels, as shown in the Max Power Level column of the Exorcist table.


You may only cast psychic powers at 6th, 7th, 8th, and 9th-level once. You regain the
ability to do so after a long rest.

**_Psycasting Ability_**

Your psycasting ability is the ability score you use to cast psychic powers. Your
psycasting ability can be either Wisdom or Charisma (your choice). You use this ability
score modifier whenever a power refers to your psycasting ability. Additionally, you use
this ability score modifier when setting the saving throw DC for a psychic power you cast
and when making an attack roll with one.

```
Psychic save DC = 8 + your proficiency bonus + your psycasting modifier
Psychic attack modifier = your proficiency bonus + your psycasting modifier
```
##### Manifest Immaterium

You can manifest your warp energies into two different effects: Revitalize and Warp
Flame. You have a pool of energy that can be used to fuel these effects, and the pool
replenishes when you take a long rest. You have a number of points in the pool equal to
your exorcist level x 5.

**_Warp Flame._** As an action, you can choose a point within 60 feet of you and draw power
from the pool to summon warp flames that deal damage up to the maximum amount
remaining in your pool. Each creature in a 10-foot radius sphere centered on that point
must make a Dexterity saving throw against your psychic save DC. Each creature within
that radius takes necrotic damage equal to the amount of points spent from your pool
on a failed save, and half as much on a successful save.

**_Revitalize._** As an action, you can touch a creature and draw power from the pool to
restore a number of hit points to that creature, up to the maximum amount remaining
in your pool. Alternatively, you can expend 5 hit points from your pool of healing to cure
the target of one disease, or neutralize one poison affecting it. You can cure multiple
diseases and neutralize multiple poisons with a single use of revitalize, expending points
separately for each one. This feature has no effect on undead and constructs. This
feature can cure all diseases, including enhanced diseases, such as Nurgle’s Rot.

##### Witch Sight

You can detect the presence of warp creatures and psykers in your vicinity. As an action,
you can open your awareness to detect such otherworldly beings. Until the end of your
next turn, you know the location of any daemon or undead within 60 feet of you that is
not behind total cover. You know the type (such as daemon or undead) of any being


whose presence you sense, but not its identity (the Daemon Primarch Angron, for
instance). Within the same radius, you also detect the presence of any creatures that
possess the psycasting feature.

You can use this feature a number of times equal to 1 + your proficiency bonus. When
you finish a long rest, you regain all expended uses.

##### Fighting Style

At 2nd level, you adopt a style of fighting as your specialty. Choose one of the following
options. You can’t take a Fighting Style option more than once, even if you later get to
choose again.

**_Blind Fighting._** You have blindsight with a range of 10 feet. Within that range, you
can effectively see anything that isn't behind total cover, even if you're blinded or in
darkness. Moreover, you can see an invisible creature within that range, unless the
creature successfully hides from you.
**_Defense._** While you are wearing armor, you gain a +1 bonus to AC.
**_Dueling._** When you are wielding a weapon in one hand and no other weapons, you
gain a +2 bonus to damage rolls with that weapon.
**_Great Weapon Fighting._** When you roll a 1 or 2 on a damage die for an attack you
make with a weapon that you are wielding with two hands, you can reroll the die and
must use the new roll, even if the new roll is a 1 or a 2. The weapon must have the two-
handed or versatile property for you to gain this benefit.
**_Interception._** When a creature you can see hits a target, other than you, within 5
feet of you with an attack, you can use your reaction to reduce the damage the target
takes by 1d10 + your proficiency bonus (to a minimum of 0 damage). You must be
wielding a shield or a simple or martial weapon to use this reaction.
**_Thrown Weapon Fighting._** You can draw a weapon that has the thrown property as
part of the attack you make with the weapon. In addition, when you hit with a ranged
attack using a thrown weapon, you gain a +2 bonus to the damage roll.
**_Two-Weapon Fighting._** When you engage in two-weapon fighting, you can add your
ability modifier to the damage of the second attack. Furthermore, being within 5 feet of
a hostile creature doesn’t impose disadvantage on your ranged attack rolls with one-
handed weapons.

##### Warp Strike

Starting at 2nd level, when you hit a creature with a melee weapon attack, you can
expend psyker points to deal additional damage to the target, and you can choose for
this additional damage to be either necrotic or radiant damage. The additional damage
is 1d8 for each point spent in this way. You can’t deal more additional damage than the


amount shown in the Warp Strike column of the Exorcist table.

The damage increases by 1d8 if the creature hit is a daemon or undead.

##### Exorcist Order

When you reach 3rd level, you begin the rite of passage to enter an order of exorcists,
and gain special features and abilities based on which order you choose, such as the
Order of Subjugation and the Order of Seers. Choose one of the options for your
exorcist order at the end of the class description.

##### Ability Score Improvement

When you reach 4th level, and again at 8th, 12th, 16th, and 19th level, you can increase
one ability score of your choice by 2, or you can increase two ability scores of your
choice by 1. As normal, you can’t increase an ability score above 20 using this feature.

##### Extra Attack

Beginning at 5th level, you can attack twice, instead of once, whenever you take the
Attack action on your turn.

##### Ritual of Purification

Starting at 5th level, you’ve studied how to exorcise creatures with a purifying rite. Over
the course of 10 minutes, you can psychically ward a 10-foot-diameter circle. When a
creature enters the circle, you can use your action to touch the creature and end any
effect causing the creature to be charmed, frightened, poisoned, possessed, and cure
the creature of all diseases. If the creature is willing, the effect ends immediately. If the
creature is not willing, it must succeed on a Charisma saving throw against your psychic
save DC, ending any of the listed effects on a failure. This ritual can purify all diseases,
including enhanced diseases, such as Nurgle’s Rot.

This feature can only end effects that are caused by a power level equal to half your
exorcist level or lower. The circle becomes inactive after 8 hours, when you create
another circle using this feature, or when you use your bonus action to deactivate the
circle. If a creature is unwilling and succeeds on the saving throw against this feature, it
becomes immune to this feature for 24 hours.

Additionally, you have learned to sanctify your body against impure effects. You have
advantage on saving throws against being possessed and against all diseases.

##### Aura of Protection


Starting at 6th level, you project a psychic aura to protect yourself or allies. Whenever
you or a friendly creature within 10 feet of you must make a saving throw, the creature
gains a bonus to the saving throw equal to your psycasting modifier (with a minimum
bonus of +1). You must be conscious to grant this bonus.

At 18th level, the range of this aura increases to 30 feet.

##### Aura of Courage

Starting at 10th level, your aura instills confidence in your allies. You and friendly
creatures within 10 feet of you can't be frightened while you are conscious.

At 18th level, the range of this aura increases to 30 feet.

##### Improved Warp Strike

By 11th level, you are so suffused with warp energy that all your melee weapon strikes
carry psychic power with them. Whenever you hit a creature with a melee weapon, the
creature takes an extra 1d8 necrotic or radiant damage (your choice). If you also use
your Warp Smite with an attack, you add this damage to the extra damage of your Warp
Smite.

##### Cleansing Touch

Beginning at 14th level, you can use your action to end one power on yourself or on one
willing creature that you touch.

You can use this feature a number of times equal to your psycasting modifier (a
minimum of once). You regain expended uses when you finish a long rest.

#### Exorcist Order

Becoming an exorcist involves completing a special rite that finally indoctrinates you
into an order, and allows you to pursue a specialization within the field of exorcism.

#### Order of Subjugation

The Order of Subjugation was created for those who walk one of the most difficult
paths: containing and controlling the creatures from beyond the veil. These exorcists
often border on the radical side, sometimes being tempted to converse and even make
pacts with the creatures that bargain for their freedom.


##### Chains of Binding

Starting at 3rd level, you can summon psychic chains to bind creatures. As a bonus
action, you can target a creature size Huge or smaller within 30 feet of you and attempt
to summon chains to bind them. The creature makes a Strength saving throw against
your psychic save DC. On a failure, the creature becomes restrained. As an action, the
chained creature can attempt a Strength saving throw, ending this effect on a success.

The chains disappear after 1 minute, if the creature succeeds against the saving throw, if
you become incapacitated, or until you end this effect early (no action required). You
can only have one creature chained at a time.

You can use this feature a number of times equal to your proficiency bonus, and you
regain all expended uses when you complete a long rest.

##### Aura of Supremacy

Starting at 7th level, you and allied creatures within 10 feet of you can’t be charmed or
possessed while you are conscious.

At 18th level, the range of this aura increases to 30 feet.

##### Searing Chains

Starting at 15th level, creatures that are restrained by your Chains of Binding take
damage at the start of their turn equal to 2d8 + your psycasting modifier. You can
choose if this damage is radiant or necrotic.

Additionally, while a creature is under the effect of your Chains of Binding, it has
disadvantage on the first saving throw to resist being banished.

##### Warden’s Avatar

Starting at 20th level, you can psychically project yourself into the avatar of the warden,
the subjugator of daemons. You gain the following benefits for 1 minute:

```
⦁ Creatures have disadvantage on saving throws and skill checks to resist and
remove your Chains of Binding.
⦁ You have resistance to all damage.
⦁ Whenever a creature damages you, it takes radiant or necrotic damage (your
choice) equal to half of the amount it dealt you.
```

#### Order of Seers

The Order of Seers are for those who use their psychic abilities to see into the world
around them and detect the weakening veil between realspace and the warp.

##### Seer’s Vision

Starting at 3rd level, when you use your witch sight, you can also detect the presence of
any illusions and powers used to hide or conceal something’s true form or nature.
Additionally, your witch sight can also detect the presence of any planar portals to the
immaterium.

##### Blessing of True Strike

Also starting at 3rd level, you can use a bonus action to bless your weapon with psychic
energies. For 1 minute, you add your psycasting ability modifier to attack rolls made
with that weapon (with a minimum bonus of +1). The weapon becomes enhanced, if it
wasn’t already. Additionally, dealing damage with this weapon to shapechangers or
creatures under the effect of an illusion causes them to make a Charisma saving throw
against your psychic save DC. On a failure, the creature reveals its true form, and any
illusions on the creature are dispelled.

You can end this effect on your turn (no action required). If you are no longer holding or
carrying this weapon, or if you become incapacitated, this effect ends. You can only
have one weapon blessed using this feature at a time.

You can use this feature a number of times equal to your proficiency bonus, and regain
all expended uses when you complete a long rest.

##### Aura of Foresight

Starting at 7th level, your aura of foresight allows your allies to act quickly in response
to danger. Allied creatures within 10 feet of you can’t be surprised, and they can add
your Psycasting modifier to their initiative rolls. These benefits last until you are
incapacitated.

At 18th level, the range of this aura increases to 30 feet.

##### Guide

Starting at 15th level, you can glimpse into the future, aiding an ally. As an action, you
can target yourself or one allied creature within 30 feet of you with this ability. Attack


rolls against this creature have disadvantage for 10 minutes.

##### Immaculate Form

Starting at 20th level, you can assume a form that can see through even the most potent
of lies. As an action, you can gain the following benefits for 1 minute:

```
⦁ You gain truesight out to 120 feet, and you know when you hear a lie.
⦁ You can cast exorcist powers that have a casting time of 1 action as a bonus
action.
⦁ You have advantage on attack rolls against all daemons.
```
## Mechnician

An ork mekboy steps forward, his body a twisted fusion of rusted metal and green skin,
before unleashing an unstable bomb towards a horde of guardsmen, turning their
bodies to ash. A tech priest looks towards the oncoming Tau fire warriors, and quickly
reveals a sphere. As he turns its dials and whispers an incantation in binary, the fire
warriors become burdened with the weight of gravity, until it crushes them and seals
them within their armor as coffins.

Mechnicians use technology as the core of their power, and then utilize its benefits in
unique ways, mastering it until they perform superhuman feats of power with its
effects.

#### Quick Build

You can make a mechnician quickly by following these suggestions. First, make
Intelligence your highest ability modifier. Your next highest score should be Dexterity or
Constitution. Second, choose the mechanic background.

#### Class Features

As a mechnician, you gain the following class features.

##### Hit Points

**Hit Dice** : 1d8 per mechnician level
**Hit Points at 1st Level** : 8 + your Constitution modifier
**Hit Points at Higher Levels** : 1d8 (or 5) + your Constitution modifier per mechnician level
after 1st


**Starting Proficiencies**
You are proficient with the following items, in addition to any proficiencies provided by
your race or background.

**Armor** : Light armor, medium armor, shields
**Weapons** : Simple weapons, martial weapons
**Tools** : Mechanic’s kit, security kit
**Saving Throws** : Dexterity, Intelligence
**Skills** : Choose three from Acrobatics, Deception, Insight, Investigation, Lore, Medicine,
Nature, Performance, Persuasion, Piloting, Sleight of Hand, and Tech.

**Starting Equipment**
You start with the following items, plus anything provided by your background.

```
⦁ (a) a rapier (b) a longsword (c) a las carbine and two power cells
⦁ (a) a diplomat's pack or (b) a technologist’s pack
⦁ (a) mesh armor or (b) trooper armor
⦁ A dagger, a las pistol and two power cells, and a security kit
```
##### The Mechnician

```
Leve
l
```
```
Proficiency
Bonus
```
```
Features Powers Known Tech Points Max Power
Level
```
###### C

```

1st +2 Critical Analysis, Techcasting 9 4 1st
```
