##### Critical Analysis

You can use your tactical skills to help allies on the battlefield and off. To do so, you use
a bonus action on your turn to choose one creature other than yourself within 60 feet of
you who can hear you. That creature gains one Critical Analysis die, a d6.

Once within the next 10 minutes, the creature can roll the die and add the number
rolled to one ability check, attack roll, or saving throw it makes. The creature can wait
until after it rolls the d20 before deciding to use the Critical Analysis die, but must
decide before the DM says whether the roll succeeds or fails. Once the Critical Analysis
die is rolled, it is lost. A creature can have only one Critical Analysis die at a time.

You can use this feature a number of times equal to your Intelligence modifier (a
minimum of once). You regain any expended uses when you finish a long rest.

Your Critical Analysis die changes when you reach certain levels in this class. The die
becomes a d8 at 5th level, a d10 at 10th level, and a d12 at 15th level.

##### Techcasting

Beginning at 1st level, you have learned to use technology to cast tech powers.

**_Tech Powers Known_**

You learn 9 tech powers of your choice, and you learn more at higher levels, as shown in
the Tech Powers Known column of the Mechnician table. You may not learn a tech
power of a level higher than your Max Power Level.

**_Tech Points_**

You have a number of tech points equal to your mechnician level x 4, as shown in the
Tech Points column of the Mechnician table. When you cast a power, you expend a
number of tech points equal to 1 + the power’s level. You regain all expended tech
points when you finish a long rest.

**_Max Power Level_**

Many tech powers can be overpowered, consuming more tech points to create a


greater effect. You can overpower these abilities to a maximum level, which increases at
higher levels, as shown in the Max Power Level column of the Mechnician table.

You may only cast tech powers at 6th, 7th, 8th, and 9th-level once. You regain the ability
to do so after a long rest.

**_Techcasting Ability_**

Your techcasting ability is the ability score you use to cast tech powers. Your techcasting
ability is Intelligence. You use this ability score modifier whenever a power refers to
your techcasting ability. Additionally, you use this ability score modifier when setting the
saving throw DC for a tech power you cast and when making an attack roll with one.

```
Tech save DC = 8 + your proficiency bonus + your techcasting modifier
Tech attack modifier = your proficiency bonus + your techcasting modifier
```
##### Cybernetic Modifications

Starting at 2nd level, you’ve learned to make modifications to your body, cybernetically
augmenting yourself. Over the course of a long rest, you can modify yourself with
cybernetic augmentations.

You have 2 modification slots, and you gain more at higher levels, as shown in the
Cybernetic Modifications column of the Mechnician table. Over the course of a long
rest, you can install, replace, or remove a number of modifications up to your
Intelligence modifier (minimum of one). The list of cybernetic modifications is listed at
the end of the class.

Some modification effects require saving throws. When you use such an effect from this
class, the DC equals your tech save DC.

##### Infuse Item

Starting at 2nd level, you gain the ability to temporarily enhance a weapon or armor by
maintaining it regularly. At the end of a long rest, you can touch one nonenhanced
object that is a suit of armor, a shield, or a simple or martial weapon. Until the end of
your next long rest, the object becomes an enhanced item, granting a +1 bonus to AC if
it’s armor or a shield or a +1 bonus to attack and damage rolls if it’s a weapon.

Once you’ve used this feature, you can’t use it again until you finish a long rest.

This bonus increases to +2 at 9th level and +3 at 13th level.


##### Mechnician School

At 3rd level, you delve into the advanced techniques of a mechnician school of your
choice. Your choice grants you features at 3rd level and again at 6th and 14th level.

##### Expertise

At 3rd level, choose two of your skill proficiencies. Your proficiency bonus is doubled for
any ability check you make that uses either of the chosen proficiencies.

At 10th level, you can choose another two skill proficiencies to gain this benefit.

##### Ability Score Improvement

When you reach 4th level, and again at 8th, 12th, 16th, and 19th level, you can increase
one ability score of your choice by 2, or you can increase two Ability Scores of your
choice by 1. As normal, you can’t increase an ability score above 20 using this feature.

##### Analytical Cogitators

Beginning when you reach 5th level, you regain all of your expended uses of Critical
Analysis when you finish a short or long rest.

##### Perfect Infusion

At 18th level, weapons you infuse score a critical strike on a roll of 19 or 20.
Alternatively, if you infuse armor, any critical hits made against it become normal hits.

##### Superior Analysis

At 20th level, you can spend one use of your Critical Analysis to give up to five allied
creatures within 30 feet of you a Critical Analysis die.

#### Mechnician Schools

Mechnicians are taught in specific schools that teach them to make and manipulate
technology. Although you may have never attended such a school, you can still adopt
the features of that school to use.

#### School of Infiltration

The school of infiltration gives its students the capabilities of stealth and manipulation,
churning out practiced spies and assassins.


##### Enable Stealth

Starting at 3rd level, you can use your action to touch a willing creature other than
yourself to give it advantage on Stealth checks. This benefit lasts for 1 hour or until you
use this feature again.

##### Self Hologram

Starting at 6th level, you can use holograms to create an illusory duplicate of yourself.

As a bonus action, you create a perfect illusion of yourself that lasts for 1 minute, or
until you lose your concentration (as if you were concentrating on a power). The illusion
appears in an unoccupied space that you can see within 30 feet of you. When you first
create this illusion and as a bonus action on each of your turns, you can move the
illusion up to 30 feet to a space you can see, but it must remain within 120 feet of you.

For the duration, you can cast powers as though you were in the illusion's space, but
you must use your own senses. Additionally, when both you and your illusion are within
5 feet of a hostile creature that can see the illusion, you have advantage on attack rolls
against that creature, given how distracting the illusion is to the target.

##### Polygram

Starting at 14th level, you can create up to four duplicates of yourself, instead of one,
when you use self hologram. When you first create these illusions and as a bonus action
on your turn, you can move any number of them up to 30 feet, to a maximum range of
120 feet.

Additionally, if one of your illusions and an allied creature are within 5 feet of a hostile
creature that can see the illusion, that allied creature has advantage on attack rolls
against the hostile creature.

#### School of Chronomancy

Few are ever allowed to see the school of chronomancy and all of the dangers that
reside within its infinite books, tomes, and data-sheets on its ever-confounding nature.
Those who dabble in technology and research regarding time and its uses via technology
are few and far in-between, and are mostly found amongst the elusive eldar and the
immortal necron.


##### Time Shift

Starting at 3rd level when you choose this school, you have learned how to use
technology to shift your position in time. You can add your Intelligence modifier to your
initiative rolls.

##### Future Glimpse

Beginning at 3rd level when you choose this school, you have the unique ability to use
technology to peer into the future and prepare for it. When you finish a long rest, roll
two d20s and record the numbers rolled. You can replace any attack roll, saving throw,
or ability check made by you or a creature that you can see with one of these foretelling
rolls. You must choose to do so before the roll, and you can replace a roll in this way
only once per turn.

Each future glimpse roll can be used only once. When you finish a long rest, you lose any
unused future glimpse rolls.

##### Stasis Field

Starting at 6th level, as a reaction to being targeted by an attack, you can cause a Large
or smaller creature attacking you that you can see to make a Constitution saving throw
against your tech save DC. On a failure, the creature is encased in a field of enhanced
energy until the end of your next turn, or until the creature takes any damage. While
encased in this way, the creature is incapacitated and has a speed of 0.

You can use this feature a number of times equal to your proficiency bonus. You regain
all expended uses when you finish a long rest.

##### Clearer Glimpse

Starting at 14th level, the visions you see intensify and paint a more accurate picture in
your mind of what is to come. You roll three d20s for your future glimpse feature, rather
than two.

#### Cybernetic Modifications

##### Optical Recorder

This augmentation replaces at least one of your eyes.

You are immune to the blinded condition, and you can enable or disable your ability to


see anytime. Additionally, your eyes are equipped with a pict recorder. You can
perfectly recall anything you’ve seen in the last 30 days.

##### Advanced Arm Augments

This augmentation replaces an arm.

When you make an ability check, attack roll, or saving throw using Strength using only
this arm, your Strength score is treated as 15. When you make an ability check, attack
roll, or saving throw using Strength using more than just this arm, you take the average
of the arm’s Strength score and your own.

You can choose this modification multiple times.

##### Advanced Leg Augments

This augmentation replaces both legs.

When determining your bonus to AC and saving throws from Dexterity, your Dexterity
score is treated as 15. If your Dexterity score is already equal to or greater than 15, it
has no effect on you.

Additionally, you can substitute this score for your own whenever you make an ability
check or attack roll that uses your legs.

##### Detachable Eye

This augmentation replaces an eye.

As an action, you can remove or replace this eye. While removed, the eye sprouts eight
small legs, has a speed of 15 feet, an AC of 10, and 1 hit point. If it dies, you can’t use it
again until you complete a long rest. As an action on each of your turns, you can move
the eye up to its speed as long as it is within 30 feet of you. You can see through both
the detached eye and your remaining eye at the same time, or you can use your action
to see through only one eye or the other.

You can choose this modification multiple times.

##### Harpoon Hand

This augmentation replaces a hand.

You modify your hand, granting it the ability to transform into a harpoon. With this


hand, you can make a ranged weapon attack with a range of 30/60. On a hit, it deals 1d6
kinetic damage. This attack can target a surface, object, or creature.

A creature struck by this attack is impaled by the harpoon. As an action, a creature can
attempt to remove the harpoon. Removing the harpoon requires an Athletics check.
While the harpoon is stuck in the target, you are connected to the target by a 60 foot
cable.

While the harpoon is deployed, you can use your bonus action to activate the reel,
pulling yourself to the location if the target is larger than you. A creature or object your
size or smaller is pulled to you. Alternatively, you can opt to release the cable (no action
required).

Once you’ve used this feature, you can’t use your hand again until you recover and
reinsert it as an action.

You can choose this modification multiple times.

##### Subdermal Armor

When you aren’t wearing armor, your AC becomes 13 + your Dexterity modifier.

##### Mechadendrite Arm

You create a mechanical arm which mounts to your shoulder, which you can use
independently. This arm can wield weapons and shields, and manipulate items and
objects as well as you can.

You can choose this modification twice.

## Psyker

The Imperial psyker stands beside the commissar, until given the signal. As he stretches
his hands outward, electricity crackles all over his body, culminating at his fingertips,
and decimates the enemies before him with the power of the warp. An eldar lays his
hands upon his fallen allies, causing restiching their wounds and bringing them back into
fighting condition. An electro priest calls forth the power of the machines, causing
electricity to surge forward and surround his enemies as they scream in pain.
Psykers manifest the power of the warp to fuel their effects, each in a variety of
ways. Psykers each have their own unique discipline that they can train themselves in,
and can even develop totally unique ways to manifest their abilities.


#### Quick Build

You can make a psyker quickly by following these suggestions. First, make Wisdom or
Charisma your highest ability modifier. Your next highest score should be Dexterity or
Constitution. Second, choose the scholar background.

#### Class Features

As a psyker, you gain the following class features.

##### Hit Points

**Hit Dice** : 1d6 per psyker level
**Hit Points at 1st Level** : 6 + your Constitution modifier
**Hit Points at Higher Levels** : 1d6 (or 4) + your Constitution modifier per psyker level after
1st

**Starting Proficiencies**
You are proficient with the following items, in addition to any proficiencies provided by
your race or background.

**Armor** : Light armor
**Weapons** : Simple weapons
**Tools** : None
**Saving Throws** : Wisdom, Charisma
**Skills** : Choose two from Deception, Insight, Intimidation, Investigation, Lore, Nature,
Occult, Performance, and Persuasion.

**Starting Equipment**
You start with the following items, plus anything provided by your Background.

```
⦁ (a) a las carbine and 2 power cells or (b) any simple weapon
⦁ (a) a dungeoneer's pack, (b) an explorer's pack, or (c) a scholar’s pack
⦁ Mesh armor and two daggers
```
##### The Psyker

##### Psycasting

You have manifested the ability to channel the immaterium to fuel your psychic powers.
See chapter 10 for the general rules of casting powers and chapter 11 for the psychic
powers list.

**_Psychic Powers Known_**

You learn 9 psychic powers of your choice, and you learn more at higher levels, as
shown in the Psychic Powers Known column of the Psyker table. You may not learn a
psychic power of a level higher than your Max Power Level.

**_Psyker Points_**

You have a number of psyker points equal to your psyker level x 4, as shown in the
Psyker Points column of the Psyker table. When you cast a power, you expend a number
of psyker points equal to 1 + the power’s level.. You regain all expended psyker points
when you finish a long rest.


**_Max Power Level_**

Many psychic powers can be overpowered, consuming more psyker points to create a
greater effect. You can overpower these abilities to a maximum level, which increases at
higher levels, as shown in the Max Power Level column of the Psyker table.

You may only cast psychic powers at 6th, 7th, 8th, and 9th-level once. You regain the
ability to do so after a long rest.

**_Psycasting Ability_**

Your psycasting ability is the ability score you use to cast psychic powers. Your
psycasting ability can be either Wisdom or Charisma (your choice). You use this ability
score modifier whenever a power refers to your psycasting ability. Additionally, you use
this ability score modifier when setting the saving throw DC for a psychic power you cast
and when making an attack roll with one.

```
Psychic save DC = 8 + your proficiency bonus + your psycasting modifier
Psychic attack modifier = your proficiency bonus + your psycasting modifier
```
##### Power Recovery

Starting at 1st level, you have learned to regain some of your energy by briefly
meditating. When you finish a short rest, you can regain a number of psyker points
equal to half your psyker level (rounded down) + your psycasting modifier. Once you’ve
used this feature, you must complete a long rest before you can use it again.

##### Warp-Empowered Casting

Starting at 2nd level, you gain the ability to manipulate the warp to fit your needs.
When you cast a psychic power, you can expend additional psyker points to modify the
power. You gain three of the following Warp-Empowered Casting options of your
choice. You gain another one at 9th and 17th level.

You can use only one Warp-Empowered Casting option on a power when you cast it,
unless otherwise noted.

**_Careful Power._** When you cast a power that forces other creatures to make a saving
throw, you can protect some of those creatures from the power’s full force. To do so,
you spend 1 psyker point and choose a number of those creatures up to your psycasting
modifier modifier (minimum of one creature). A chosen creature automatically succeeds
on its saving throw against the power.
**_Distant Power._** When you cast a power that has a range of 5 feet or greater, you can


spend 1 additional psyker point to double the range of the power. When you cast a
power that has a range of touch, you can spend 1 additional psyker point to make the
range of the power 30 feet.
**_Extended Power._** When you cast a power that has a duration of 1 minute or longer,
you can spend 1 psyker point to double its duration, to a maximum duration of 24
hours.
**_Heightened Power._** When you cast a power that forces a creature to make a saving
throw to resist its effects, you can spend 3 psyker points to give one target of the power
disadvantage on its first saving throw made against the power.
**_Improved Power._** When you roll damage for a power, you can spend 1 additional
psyker point to reroll a number of the damage dice up to your psycasting modifier
(minimum of one). You must use the new rolls. You can use Improved Power even if you
have already used a different Warp-Empowered Casting option during the casting of the
power.
**_Quickened Power._** When you cast a power that has a casting time of 1 action, you
can spend 2 psyker points to change the casting time to 1 bonus action for this casting.
**_Seeking Power._** If you miss with a psychic power that calls for an attack roll, you can
spend 2 psyker points to reroll the attack. You must use the new roll. You can use
Seeking Power even if you have already used a different Force-Empowered Casting
option during the casting of the power.
**_Twinned Power._** When you cast a power that targets only one creature and doesn’t
have a range of self, you can spend a number of psyker points equal to the power’s level
to target a second creature in range with the same power (1 psyker point if it is an at-
will power). To be eligible, a power must be incapable of targeting more than one
creature at the power’s current level. For example, _scorching ray_ aren’t eligible, but _ray
of frost_ is.

##### Telekinetic Barrier

Starting at 2nd level, you can summon a telekinetic barrier of psychic energy to repel
attacks. When you are hit by an attack, you can use your reaction to create a barrier of
psychic energy. Until the start of your next turn, you have a bonus to AC equal to your
psycasting modifier (minimum of +1). This includes the triggering attack.

You can use this feature a number of times equal to your proficiency bonus, as shown in
the Psyker table. You regain all expended uses when you finish a long rest.

##### Psychic Discipline

Starting at 3rd level, you begin specialized training on a psychic discipline of your choice.

Your choice grants you features when you choose it at 3rd level and again at 6th, 14th,
and 18th level.


##### Ability Score Improvement

When you reach 4th level, and again at 8th, 12th, 16th, and 19th level, you can increase
one ability score of your choice by 2, or you can increase two Ability Scores of your
choice by 1. As normal, you can’t increase an ability score above 20 using this feature.

##### Psychic Mastery

At 20th level, your attunement to the immaterium has become absolute. You gain
mastery over two psychic powers, and can cast them with little effort. Choose two 3rd-
level psychic powers that you know as your mastered powers. You can cast each of
these powers once as 3rd-level powers without expending psyker points. Once you cast
a mastered power in this way, you can’t cast that power again until you complete a
short or long rest.

If you want to cast it at a higher level, you must expend psyker points as normal.

#### Psychic Disciplines

After amounting enough power, a psyker may dedicate themselves to psychic discipline
to hone their strengths. These disciplines define a psyker’s main strengths, and may
even be able to be used to gain favor with certain factions.

#### Biomancy

The discipline of biomancy focuses on the body, and using psychic powers to influence
the physical attributes of one’s body.

##### Puppet Body

At 3rd level when you choose this discipline, you can control the flow of blood and
muscles in a creature. As a bonus action, you target a Large or smaller creature that has
blood or muscles within 60 feet of you. That creature must succeed on a Constitution
saving throw against your psychic save DC or immediately move up to half of their
movement in any direction of your choice and make a single weapon attack against a
creature of your choice within range. Dead or unconscious creatures automatically fail
their saving throw.

You can use this feature a number of times equal to your proficiency bonus, and you
regain all expended uses when you finish a long rest.


##### Psychic Stitches

Starting at 3rd level, you gain the ability to stitch wounds back together. When you cast
a psychic power that restores hit points, you can re-roll any results of 1 or 2 on the die,
accepting the new roll.

##### Crystallize Blood

At 6th level, you can cause blood to crystallize as it leaves the wound, dealing damage to
its attacker. As a reaction to a creature that has blood within 30 feet of you taking
damage, you can cause the attacker to take piercing damage equal to 1d6 + your
psycasting modifier.

At 14th level, this deals an additional 2d6 piercing damage.

You can use this feature a number of times equal to your psycasting modifier, and you
regain all expended uses at the end of a long rest.

##### Burst Veins

At 17th level, as an action, you can emit a powerful aura that extends 30 feet out from
you. This aura pulses necrotic energy through the veins of nearby foes, causing them to
burst and bleed.

For 1 minute, any hostile creatures with blood that begin their turn within the aura or
enter it for the first time on their turn immediately suffer 2d6 necrotic damage. Any
hostile creature with blood that would regain hit points while within the aura only
regains half of the intended number of hit points.

Once you use this feature, you can’t use it again until you finish a long rest.

#### Technomancy

The art of technomancy is followed by the psykers with the Cult of the Mechanicum,
otherwise known as electro priests. Other psykers who practice technomancy are often
found working closely alongside technology, and even the Dark Mechanicum has their
versions of electro priests. Those who follow this art have the ability to manipulate
machinery with their psychic ability.

##### One With Electricity

Starting at 3rd level when you choose this discipline, you gain resistance to lightning


damage.

##### Haywire Pulse

Also at 3rd level, you gain the ability to psychically render electronic devices inoperable.
As an action, you can target one electronic device within range that is not an artifact,
causing the device to shut down.. If the device is being held or operated by a creature,
the creature must succeed on an Intelligence saving throw to stop the device from being
shut down. Until the end of your next turn, the device can’t start or be restarted while
the targeted device is within range.

You can use this feature a number of times equal to your proficiency bonus, and you
regain all expended uses when you complete a long rest.

##### Wire Travel

At 6th level, you gain the ability to psychically travel short distances over electric wires
such as data lines, power cables, and telephone wires. As a bonus action, you can touch
a device or outlet connected to a hardwired network and teleport along this network to
another device or outlet within your line of sight, up to a maximum distance of one mile
away, ending up in the nearest unoccupied space near the targeted location.

Once you use this feature, you can’t use it again until you finish a short or long rest.

##### Sense Network

At 14th level, when you touch an electronic device, wire, or outlet, you can psychically
sense up to a range of 300 feet all the hardwired connections the device has made to it.
This allows you to know the specific location and direction of all hardwired connections,
but not necessarily what it is connected to, nor what is in the location it is connected to.
For example, you can detect that a computer is connected to an outlet going 100 feet to
the north-west, but not that the room 100 feet to the north-west is a surveillance room.

Additionally, your Wire Travel can teleport you and up to five creatures of your choice
within 5 feet of you along electronic wires, and you can teleport to locations that you
can sense through this feature, teleporting you and any creatures along with you to the
nearest unoccupied space at the end of the connection.

##### Curse of the Machine Spirits

At 18th level, you can disable technology at a whim. Choose up to five items or devices
within 60 feet that you can see that are not artifacts. For 1 hour, these items lose any


enhanced benefits, and the item is turned off. These items can’t be restarted or turned
back on during this time, but a creature can attempt to restart the device by using their
action to make an Intelligence check against your psychic save DC, successfully
activating the device on a success.

Once you use this feature, you can’t use it again until you complete a long rest.

## Renegade

A ratling spy takes a moment, adjusting his night vision goggles. Tracing the outline of
the room with his eyes, he nimbly steps over the now-visible sensors lining the ground,
reaching the main console of the room. Within a moment, he reveals a selection of tools
and begins prying and pulling out cogitators and cogs until the machine gives a final
squeak and ceases to function. Shoving the tools back in his pockets, he watches over
his dataslate as his allies breach the facility’s doors, guns blazing.

A kroot stalks through the thick jungles, finding a thin-bladed leaf, a tinge of blood on its
one droplet. Silently, he climbs up the trunk of a tree, peering out over the distance to
see the camp of guardsmen he has been following for days. He trills to himself in delight
as he lowers his kroot rifle and steadies his shot.

The Tau caste dances before the haughty Imperial nobles, their faces flushed red with
bottles of wine littering the room. As the show ends and the music dies down, the lights
shut off, only for the Tau to unsheathe the dagger hidden inside of her boot, quickly
dashing across the room, mixing blood with wine.

Renegades, whether good, bad, or neutral, are those who focus on a specific practice
and utilize it to get the upper hand. They can come from any world or region in the
galaxy, with origins from the lowliest scoundrel to the social elite, from craven gangers
to respected spies.

#### Quick Build

You can make a renegade quickly by following these suggestions. First, make Dexterity
your highest ability modifier. Your next highest score should be Intelligence or Charisma.
Second, choose the criminal background.

#### Class Features

As a renegade, you gain the following class features.


##### Hit Points

**Hit Dice** : 1d8 per renegade level
**Hit Points at 1st Level** : 8 + your Constitution modifier
**Hit Points at Higher Levels** : 1d8 (or 5) + your Constitution modifier per renegade level
after 1st

**Starting Proficiencies**
You are proficient with the following items, in addition to any proficiencies provided by
your race or background.

**Armor** : Light armor
**Weapons** : Simple weapons, martial weapons
**Tools** : Security kit
**Saving Throws** : Dexterity, Intelligence
**Skills** : Choose four from Acrobatics, Deception, Insight, Intimidation, Investigation, Lore,
Perception, Performance, Persuasion, Piloting, Sleight of Hand, Survival, and Tech.

**Starting Equipment**
You start with the following items, plus anything provided by your background.

```
⦁ (a) a rapier or (b) a shortsword
⦁ (a) a pistol and 2 magazines or (b) a shortsword
⦁ (a) a burglar's pack, (b) a dungeoneer's pack, or (c) an explorer's pack
⦁ Mesh armor, two daggers, and a security kit
```
##### The Renegade

```
Level Proficiency
Bonus
```

```
Features Sneak Attack
```

```
7th +3 Evasion 4d6
8th +3 Ability Score Improvement 4d6
9th +4 Roguish Archetype feature 5d6
10th +4 Ability Score Improvement 5d6
```

```
11th +4 Reliable Talent 6d6
12th +4 Ability Score Improvement 6d6
13th +5 Roguish Archetype feature 7d6
14th +5 Blindsense 7d6
15th +5 Slippery Mind 8d6
16th +5 Ability Score Improvement 8d6
17th +6 Roguish Archetype feature 9d6
18th +6 Elusive 9d6
19th +6 Ability Score Improvement 10d6
20th +6 Stroke of Luck 10d6
```
##### Expertise

At 1st level, choose two of your skill proficiencies, or one of your skill proficiencies and
your proficiency with a security kit. Your proficiency bonus is doubled for any ability
check you make that uses either of the chosen proficiencies.

At 6th level, you can choose two more of your proficiencies (in skills or with the security
kit) to gain this benefit.

##### Sneak Attack

Beginning at 1st level, you know how to strike subtly and exploit a foe's distraction.
Once per turn, you can deal an extra 1d6 damage to one creature you hit with an attack
if you have advantage on the attack roll. The attack must use a finesse or a ranged
weapon.

You don't need advantage on the attack roll if another enemy of the target is within 5
feet of it, that enemy isn't incapacitated, and you don't have disadvantage on the attack
roll.

The amount of the extra damage increases as you gain levels in this class, as shown in
the Sneak Attack column of the Renegade table.

##### Cunning Action

Starting at 2nd level, your quick thinking and agility allow you to move and act quickly.
You can take a bonus action on each of your turns in combat. This action can be used
only to take the Dash, Disengage, or Hide action.

##### Roguish Archetype

At 3rd level, you choose an archetype that you emulate in the exercise of your renegade


abilities, such as Thief. Your archetype choice grants you features at 3rd level and then
again at 9th, 13th, and 17th level.

##### Ability Score Improvement

When you reach 4th level, and again at 8th, 10th, 12th, 16th, and 19th level, you can
increase one ability score of your choice by 2, or you can increase two Ability Scores of
your choice by 1. As normal, you can’t increase an ability score above 20 using this
feature.

##### Uncanny Dodge

Starting at 5th level, when an attacker that you can see hits you with an attack, you can
use your reaction to halve the attack's damage against you.

##### Evasion

Beginning at 7th level, you can nimbly dodge out of the way of certain area effects, such
as a dreadnought’s _barrage_ or an _ice storm_ power. When you are subjected to an effect
that allows you to make a Dexterity saving throw to take only half damage, you instead
take no damage if you succeed on the saving throw, and only half damage if you fail.

##### Reliable Talent

By 11th level, you have refined your chosen skills until they approach perfection.
Whenever you make an ability check that lets you add your proficiency bonus, you can
treat a d20 roll of 9 or lower as a 10.

##### Blindsense

Starting at 14th level, if you are able to hear, you are aware of the location of any
hidden or invisible creature within 10 feet of you.

##### Slippery Mind

By 15th level, your cunning grants you greater mental flexibility. You gain proficiency in
Wisdom saving throws. If you already have proficiency in Wisdom saving throws, you
can choose another saving throw to gain proficiency in.

##### Elusive

Beginning at 18th level, you are so evasive that attackers rarely gain the upper hand
against you. No attack roll has advantage against you while you aren't Incapacitated.


##### Stroke of Luck

At 20th level, you have an uncanny knack for succeeding when you need to. If your
attack misses a target within range, you can turn the miss into a hit. Alternatively, if you
fail an ability check, you can treat The D20 roll as a 20.

Once you use this feature, you can't use it again until you finish a short or long rest.

#### Renegade Archetypes

Renegades have many features in common, but are highly specialized based on their
archetypes. These archetypes reflect their true training, such as being an assassin, spy,
or burglar.

#### Thief

You hone your skills in the larcenous arts. Burglars, bandits, cutpurses, and other
criminals typically follow this archetype, but so do renegades who prefer to think of
themselves as professional treasure seekers, explorers, delvers, and investigators. In
addition to improving your agility and stealth, you learn skills useful for delving into
ancient ruins, reading unfamiliar languages, and using enhanced items you normally
couldn’t employ.

##### Fast Hands

Starting at 3rd level, you can use the bonus action granted by your Cunning Action to
make a Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) check, use your security kit to disarm a trap or open a
lock, or take the Use an Object action.

##### Second-Story Work

When you choose this archetype at 3rd level, you gain the ability to climb faster than
normal; climbing no longer costs you extra movement.

In addition, when you make a running jump, the distance you cover increases by a
number of feet equal to your Dexterity modifier.

##### Supreme Sneak

Starting at 9th level, you have advantage on a Dexterity (Stealth) check if you move no
more than half your speed on the same turn.


##### Use Device

By 13th level, you have learned enough about the workings of technology and exotic
items that you can improvise the use of items even when they are not intended for you.
You ignore all class, race, and level requirements on the use of enhanced and psychic
items.

##### Thief’s Reflexes

When you reach 17th level, you have become adept at laying ambushes and quickly
escaping danger. You can take two turns during the first round of any combat. You take
your first turn at your normal initiative and your second turn at your Initiative minus 10.
You can’t use this feature when you are surprised.

#### Assassin

Assassins are dedicated to the craft of hunting their target down, and killing them as
quickly as possible.

##### Bonus Proficiencies

When you choose this archetype at 3rd level, you gain proficiency with the disguise kit
and the poisoner’s kit.

##### Assassinate

Starting at 3rd level, you are at your deadliest when you get the drop on your enemies.
You have advantage on attack rolls against any creature that hasn't taken a turn in the
combat yet. In addition, any hit you score against a creature that is surprised is a critical
hit.

##### Infiltration Expertise

Starting at 9th level, you can unfailingly create false identities for yourself. You must
spend seven days and 25 gp to establish the history, profession, and affiliations for an
identity. You can't establish an identity that belongs to someone else. For example, you
might acquire appropriate clothing, letters of introduction, and official-looking
certification to establish yourself as a member of a trading house from a remote city so
you can insinuate yourself into the company of other wealthy merchants.

Thereafter, if you adopt the new identity as a disguise, other creatures believe you to be


that person until given an obvious reason not to.

##### Imposter

At 13th level, you gain the ability to unerringly mimic another person's speech, writing,
and behavior. You must spend at least three hours studying these three components of
the person's behavior, listening to speech, examining handwriting, and observing
mannerisms.

Your ruse is indiscernible to the casual observer. If a wary creature suspects something
is amiss, you have advantage on any Charisma (Deception) check you make to avoid
detection.

##### Death Strike

Starting at 17th level, you become a master of instant death. When you attack and hit a
creature that is surprised, it must make a Constitution saving throw (DC 8 + your
Dexterity modifier + your proficiency bonus). On a failed save, double the damage of
your attack against the creature.

## Soldier

As the sounds of artillery pounding the trenches looms ahead, the guardsmen press on,
bayonets at the ready, forever forced to engage the enemy. The Tau fire warriors
unload a barrage of blue energy from their weapons as they pound into the onslaught of
strange, red-skinned creatures that seemed to spawn out of nowhere. Space marines
march in total unison towards the overwhelming force of thousands of tyranids charging
in their direction.
From the stalwart space marines, to the humble guardsmen, to mercenaries,
assassins, and even tribal warriors vying for supremacy against nature, the soldier
makes up the common rank-and-file man that fights for a purpose.

#### Quick Build

You can make a soldier quickly by following these suggestions. First, make Strength or
Dexterity your highest ability modifier, depending if you want to focus on melee or
ranged combat (or finesse weapons). Your next highest score should be Constitution.
Second, choose the military background.


#### Class Features

As a soldier, you gain the following class features.

##### Hit Points

**Hit Dice** : 1d10 per soldier level
**Hit Points at 1st Level** : 10 + your Constitution modifier
**Hit Points at Higher Levels** : 1d10 (or 6) + your Constitution modifier per soldier level
after 1st

**Starting Proficiencies**
You are proficient with the following items, in addition to any proficiencies provided by
your race or background.

**Armor** : Light armor, medium armor, heavy armor, shields
**Weapons** : Simple weapons, martial weapons
**Tools** : None
**Saving Throws** : Strength, Constitution
**Skills** : Choose two skills from Acrobatics, Athletics, Insight, Intimidation, Lore,
Perception, Piloting, and Survival.

**Starting Equipment**
You start with the following items, plus anything provided by your background.

```
⦁ (a) battle armor or (b) mesh armor, assault rifle, and two magazines
⦁ (a) a martial weapon and a shield or (b) two martial weapons
⦁ (a) a las carbine and two power cells or (b) two handaxes
⦁ (a) a dungeoneer's pack or (b) an explorer's pack
```
##### The Soldier

```
Level Proficiency
Bonus
```
```
Features
```
```
1st +2 Fighting Style, Second Wind
2nd +2 Action Surge (one use)
3rd +2 Soldier Doctrine
4th +2 Ability Score Improvement
5th +3 Extra Attack
6th +3 Ability Score Improvement
```

```
7th +3 Soldier Doctrine feature
8th +3 Ability Score Improvement
9th +4 Indomitable (one use)
10th +4 Soldier Doctrine feature
11th +4 Extra Attack (2)
12th +4 Ability Score Improvement
13th +5 Indomitable (two uses)
14th +5 Ability Score Improvement
15th +5 Soldier Doctrine feature
16th +5 Ability Score Improvement
17th +6 Action Surge (two uses), Indomitable (three uses)
18th +6 Soldier Doctrine feature
19th +6 Ability Score Improvement
20th +6 Extra Attack ( 3)
```
##### Fighting Style

You adopt a particular style of fighting as your specialty. Choose a Fighting Style from
the list of optional features. You can't take the same Fighting Style option more than
once, even if you get to choose again.

**_Blind Fighting._** You have blindsight with a range of 10 feet. Within that range, you
can effectively see anything that isn't behind total cover, even if you're blinded or in
darkness. Moreover, you can see an invisible creature within that range, unless the
creature successfully hides from you.
**_Defense._** While you are wearing armor, you gain a +1 bonus to AC.
**_Dueling._** When you are wielding a weapon in one hand and no other weapons, you
gain a +2 bonus to damage rolls with that weapon.
**_Great Weapon Fighting._** When you roll a 1 or 2 on a damage die for an attack you
make with a weapon that you are wielding with two hands, you can reroll the die and
must use the new roll, even if the new roll is a 1 or a 2. The weapon must have the two-
handed or versatile property for you to gain this benefit.
**_Interception._** When a creature you can see hits a target, other than you, within 5
feet of you with an attack, you can use your reaction to reduce the damage the target
takes by 1d10 + your proficiency bonus (to a minimum of 0 damage). You must be
wielding a shield or a simple or martial weapon to use this reaction.
**_Superior Technique._** You learn one maneuver of your choice from among those
available to the Battle Master archetype. If a maneuver you use requires your target to
make a saving throw to resist the maneuver’s effects, the saving throw DC equals 8 +
your proficiency bonus + your Strength or Dexterity modifier (your choice).
You gain one superiority die, which is a d6 (this die is added to any superiority dice


you have from another source). This die is used to fuel your maneuvers. A superiority
die is expended when you use it. You regain your expended superiority dice when you
finish a short or long rest.
**_Thrown Weapon Fighting._** You can draw a weapon that has the thrown property as
part of the attack you make with the weapon. In addition, when you hit with a ranged
attack using a thrown weapon, you gain a +2 bonus to the damage roll.
**_Two-Weapon Fighting._** When you engage in two-weapon fighting, you can add your
ability modifier to the damage of the second attack. Furthermore, being within 5 feet of
a hostile creature doesn’t impose disadvantage on your ranged attack rolls with one-
handed weapons.
**_Unarmed Fighting._** Your unarmed strikes can deal bludgeoning damage equal to 1d6
+ your Strength modifier on a hit. If you aren’t wielding any weapons or a shield when
you make the attack roll, the d6 becomes a d8. At the start of each of your turns, you
can deal 1d4 bludgeoning damage to one creature grappled by you.

##### Second Wind

You have a limited well of stamina that you can draw on to protect yourself from harm.
On your turn, you can use a bonus action to regain hit points equal to 1d10 + your
soldier level. Once you use this feature, you must finish a short or long rest before you
can use it again.

##### Action Surge

Starting at 2nd level, you can push yourself beyond your normal limits for a moment. On
your turn, you can take one additional action on top of your regular action and a
possible bonus action.

Once you use this feature, you must finish a short or long rest before you can use it
again. Starting at 17th level, you can use it twice before a rest, but only once on the
same turn.

##### Soldier Doctrine

At 3rd level, you choose the doctrine that shapes your abilities as a soldier. The
archetype you choose grants you features at 3rd level and again at 7th, 10th, 15th, and
18th level.

##### Ability Score Improvement

When you reach 4th level, and again at 6th, 8th, 12th, 14th, 16th, and 19th level, you
can increase one ability score of your choice by 2, or you can increase two ability scores
of your choice by 1. As normal, you can’t increase an ability score above 20 using this


feature.

##### Extra Attack

Beginning at 5th level, you can attack twice, instead of once, whenever you take the
attack action on your turn.

The number of attacks increases to three when you reach 11th level in this class and to
four when you reach 20th level in this class.

##### Indomitable

Beginning at 9th level, you can reroll a saving throw that you fail. If you do so, you must
use the new roll, and you can't use this feature again until you finish a long rest.

You can use this feature twice between long rests starting at 13th level and three times
between long rests starting at 17th level.

#### Soldier Doctrines

Different soldiers have different doctrines they train for to adapt to war. The soldier
doctrine you choose reflects your training and adaptations you have personally
undertaken for war.

#### Battle Master

The battle masters are those who employ a variety of maneuvers to devastate and
control the battlefield to their whims. These soldiers have a tool for every situation, and
seldom come unprepared.

##### Combat Superiority

When you choose this archetype at 3rd level, you learn maneuvers that are fueled by
special dice called superiority dice.

**_Maneuvers._** You learn three maneuvers of your choice. Many maneuvers enhance an
attack in some way. You can use only one maneuver per attack. You learn two additional
maneuvers of your choice at 7th, 10th, and 15th level. Each time you learn new
maneuvers, you can also replace one maneuver you know with a different one.

**_Superiority Dice._** You have four superiority dice, which are d8s. A superiority die is
expended when you use it. You regain all of your expended superiority dice when you
finish a short or long rest. You gain another superiority die at 7th level and one more at


15th level.

**_Saving Throws._** Some of your maneuvers require your target to make a saving throw to
resist the maneuver's effects. The saving throw DC is calculated as follows:

```
Maneuver save DC = 8 + your proficiency bonus + your Strength or Dexterity modifier
(your choice)
```
##### Student of War

At 3rd level, you gain proficiency with one type of artisan's tools or tech gadget of your
choice.

##### Know Your Enemy

Starting at 7th level, if you spend at least 1 minute observing or interacting with another
creature outside combat, you can learn certain information about its capabilities
compared to your own. The DM tells you if the creature is your equal, superior, or
inferior in regard to two of the following characteristics of your choice:

```
⦁ Strength score
⦁ Dexterity score
⦁ Constitution score
⦁ Armor Class
⦁ Current hit points
⦁ Total class levels, if any
⦁ Soldier class levels, if any
```
##### Improved Combat Superiority

At 10th level, your superiority dice turn into d10s. At 18th level, they turn into d12s.

##### Relentless

Starting at 15th level, when you roll initiative and have no superiority dice remaining,
you regain 1 superiority die.

##### Battle Master Maneuvers

**_Ambush._** When you make a Dexterity (Stealth) check or an initiative roll, you can
expend one superiority die and add the die to the roll.
**_Bait and Switch._** When you’re within 5 feet of an ally on your turn, you can expend
one superiority die and switch places with that ally, provided you spend at least 5 feet of


movement. This movement doesn’t provoke opportunity attacks. Roll the superiority
die. Until the start of your next turn, the ally gains a bonus to AC equal to the number
rolled.
**_Brace._** When an enemy you can see moves within 5 feet of you, you can use your
reaction to expend one superiority die and make one weapon attack against that
creature. If the attack hits, add the superiority die to the attack’s damage roll.
**_Distracting Strike._** When you hit a creature with a weapon attack, you can expend
one superiority die to distract the creature, giving your allies an opening. You add the
superiority die to the attack's damage roll. The next attack roll against the target by an
attacker other than you has advantage if the attack is made before the start of your next
turn.
**_Evasive Footwork._** When you move, you can expend one superiority die, rolling the
die and adding the number rolled to your AC until you stop moving.
**_Goading Attack._** When you hit a creature with a weapon attack, you can expend one
superiority die to attempt to goad the target into attacking you. You add the superiority
die to the attack's damage roll, and the target must make a Wisdom saving throw. On a
failed save, the target has disadvantage on all attack rolls against targets other than you
until the end of your next turn.
**_Maneuvering Attack._** When you hit a creature with a weapon attack, you can
expend one superiority die to maneuver one of your comrades into a more
advantageous position. You add the superiority die to the attack's damage roll, and you
choose a friendly creature who can see or hear you. That creature can use its reaction to
move up to half its speed without provoking opportunity attacks from the target of your
attack.
**_Menacing Attack._** When you hit a creature with a weapon attack, you can expend
one superiority die to attempt to frighten the target. You add the superiority die to the
attack's damage roll, and the target must make a Wisdom saving throw. On a failed
save, it is frightened of you until the end of your next turn.
**_Parry._** When another creature damages you with a melee attack, you can use your
reaction and expend one superiority die to reduce the damage by the number you roll
on your superiority die + your Dexterity modifier.
**_Precision Attack._** When you make a weapon attack roll against a creature, you can
expend one superiority die to add it to the roll. You can use this maneuver before or
after making the attack roll, but before any effects of the attack are applied.
**_Pushing Attack._** When you hit a creature with a weapon attack, you can expend one
superiority die to attempt to drive the target back. You add the superiority die to the
attack's damage roll, and if the target is large or smaller, it must make a Strength saving
throw. On a failed save, you push the target up to 15 feet away from you.
**_Riposte._** When a creature misses you with a melee attack, you can use your reaction
and expend one superiority die to make a melee weapon attack against the creature. If
you hit, you add the superiority die to the attack's damage roll.


**_Silver Tongue._** When you make a Deception check or a Persuasion check, you can
expend one superiority die, and add the superiority die to the ability check.
**_Studious Eye._** When you make an Insight check or an Investigation check, you can
expend one superiority die, and add the superiority die to the ability check.
**_Sweeping Attack._** When you hit a creature with a melee weapon attack, you can
expend one superiority die to attempt to damage another creature with the same
attack. Choose another creature within 5 feet of the original target and within your
reach. If the original attack roll would hit the second creature, it takes damage equal to
the number you roll on your superiority die. The damage is of the same type dealt by
the original attack.
**_Technical Knock._** When you make a Piloting check or a Tech check, you can expend
one superiority dice, and add the superiority die to the ability check.
**_Trip Attack._** When you hit a creature with a weapon attack, you can expend one
superiority die to attempt to knock the target down. You add the superiority die to the
attack's damage roll, and if the target is large or smaller, it must make a Strength saving
throw. On a failed save, you knock the target prone

#### Champion

Champions are those who forward their cause with extreme efficiency. From the
daunting champions of Chaos to the humble guardsman, these champions offer fury and
might to whomever they fight alongside.

##### Improved Critical

Beginning when you choose this archetype at 3rd level, your weapon attacks score a
critical hit on a roll of 19 or 20.

##### Remarkable Athlete

Starting at 7th level, you can add half your proficiency bonus (rounded up) to any
Strength, Dexterity, or Constitution check you make that doesn't already use your
proficiency bonus.

In addition, when you make a running long jump, the distance you can cover increases
by a number of feet equal to your Strength modifier.

##### Additional Fighting Style

At 10th level, you can choose a second option from the Fighting Style class feature.


##### Superior Critical

Starting at 15th level, your weapon attacks score a critical hit on a roll of 18-20.

##### Survivor

At 18th level, you attain the pinnacle of resilience in battle. At the start of each of your
turns, you regain hit points equal to 5 + your Constitution modifier if you have no more
than half of your hit points left. You don't gain this benefit if you have 0 hit points.

## Sorcerer

The tainted human reaches his hands upwards to the sky, summoning a colossal ball of
flame. Looking down at the feeble guardsmen sprawled out before him, their lasguns
shaking, he hurls the ball of flame before them, leaving naught but ash and dust in his
wake.

Sorcerers are psykers, but have the powers of the warp augmented by a daemon or
other being in the warp they have made a pact with. Some sorcerers might have made
pacts with less-maligned beings, such as with the rare living saint, but the vast majority
of them all have their powers from the daemons that watch over them.

#### Quick Build

You can make a sorcerer quickly by following these suggestions. First, make Wisdom or
Charisma your highest ability score. Your next highest score should be Dexterity or
Constitution. Second, choose the heretic background.

#### Class Features

As a sorcerer, you gain the following class features.

##### Hit Points

**Hit Dice** : 1d6 per sorcerer level
**Hit Points at 1st Level** : 6 + your Constitution modifier
**Hit Points at Higher Levels** : 1d6 (or 4) + your Constitution modifier per sorcerer level
after 1st

**Starting Proficiencies**


You are proficient with the following items, in addition to any proficiencies provided by
your race or background.

**Armor** : Light armor
**Weapons** : Simple weapons
**Tools** : None
**Saving Throws** : Wisdom, Charisma
**Skills** : Choose two skills from Deception, Intimidation, Investigation, Lore, Nature,
Occult, Performance, and Persuasion.

**Starting Equipment**
You start with the following items, plus anything provided by your background.

```
⦁ (a) a las carbine and 2 power cells or (b) any simple weapon
⦁ (a) a scholar's pack or (b) a priest’s pack
⦁ Mesh armor, any simple weapon, and two daggers
```
##### The Sorcerer

##### Otherworldly Patron

At 1st level, you have struck a bargain with an otherworldly being of your choice, such
as the Changer of Ways, or the Great Unclean One. Although patrons are most often
daemons, your patron might even be a powerful daemon primarch, a lesser daemon of
immense influence, a living saint, or even another sorcerer of unimaginable power. Your
choice grants you features at 1st level and again at 6th, 10th, and 14th level.

##### Psycasting

You have manifested the ability to channel the immaterium to fuel your psychic powers.
See chapter 10 for the general rules of casting powers and chapter 11 for the psychic
powers list.

**_Psychic Powers Known_**

You learn 9 psychic powers of your choice, and you learn more at higher levels, as
shown in the Psychic Powers Known column of the Sorcerer table. You may not learn a
psychic power of a level higher than your Max Power Level.

**_Psyker Points_**

You have a number of psyker points equal to your psyker level x 4, as shown in the
Psyker Points column of the Sorcerer table. When you cast a power, you expend a
number of psyker points equal to 1 + the power’s level. You regain all expended psyker
points when you finish a long rest.

**_Max Power Level_**

Many psychic powers can be overpowered, consuming more psyker points to create a
greater effect. You can overpower these abilities to a maximum level, which increases at
higher levels, as shown in the Max Power Level column of the Psyker table.

You may only cast psychic powers at 6th, 7th, 8th, and 9th-level once. You regain the
ability to do so after a long rest.

**_Psycasting Ability_**

Your psycasting ability is the ability score you use to cast psychic powers. Your


psycasting ability can be either Wisdom or Charisma (your choice). You use this ability
score modifier whenever a power refers to your psycasting ability. Additionally, you use
this ability score modifier when setting the saving throw DC for a psychic power you cast
and when making an attack roll with one.

```
Psychic save DC = 8 + your proficiency bonus + your psycasting modifier
Psychic attack modifier = your proficiency bonus + your psycasting modifier
```
##### Eldritch Invocations

In your study of occult lore, you have unearthed eldritch invocations, fragments of
forbidden knowledge that imbue you with an abiding unnatural ability.

At 2nd level, you gain two eldritch invocations of your choice. Your invocation options
are detailed at the end of the class description. When you gain certain sorcerer levels,
you gain additional invocations of your choice.

Additionally, when you gain a level in this class, you can choose one of the invocations
you know and replace it with another invocation that you could learn at that level. A
level prerequisite in an invocation refers to sorcerer level, not character level.

##### Pact Familiar

At 3rd level, your otherworldly patron bestows a loyal familiar for your service. You
learn the _summon familiar_ psychic power. The power doesn’t count against your
number of powers known.
When you cast this power, you can choose one of the normal forms for your familiar
or use the following special form, listed below, detailed in the Pact Familiar stat block.
You choose what this creature looks like. For example, a sorcerer of the Great Unclean
One might have his familiar take the form of a nurgling, while a sorcerer of the Changer
of Ways might have a blue horror as his familiar.

### Pact Familiar

```
Tiny daemon, any alignment
Armor Class 11 + your proficiency bonus
Hit Points 10 + your sorcerer level
Speed 30 ft., fly 60 ft.
STR
6 (-2)
```
```
DEX
17 (+3)
```
```
CON
12 (+1)
```
```
INT
12 (+1)
```
```
WIS
12 (+1)
```
```
CHA
14 (+2)
```

```
Skills: Perception +1 plus PB, Stealth +3 plus PB x 2
Damage Resistances: cold; energy and kinetic damage from
nonenhanced attacks that aren’t blessed.
Damage Immunities: fire, poison
Condition Immunities : exhaustion, poisoned
Senses: darkvision 120 ft., passive Perception 11 plus PB
Languages: speaks the languages of its summoner
Proficiency Bonus (PB): equals your bonus
Shapechanger: The familiar can use its action to polymorph into a beast
that resembles a rat (speed 20 ft.), a raven (20 ft., fly 60 ft.), or a spider (20
ft., climb 20 ft.), or back into its true form. Its statistics are the same in each
form, except for the speed changes noted. Any equipment it is wearing or
carrying isn’t transformed. It reverts to its true form if it dies.
```
```
Unholy Sight. Enhanced darkness doesn’t impede the familiar’s
darkvision.
```
```
Psychic Resistance. The familiar has advantage on Wisdom and
Charisma saving throws against psychic powers.
```
```
Pact Knowledge. While the familiar is on the same plane of existence as
its master, the master has advantage on Wisdom (Occult) checks.
```
#### ACTIONS

```
Bite. Melee Weapon Attack: your psychic attack bonus to hit, reach 5 ft.,
one target. Hit: 1d6+3+your psycasting modifier kinetic damage.
```
```
Invisibility. The familiar psychically turns invisible until it attacks or until its
concentration ends (as if it were concentrating on a power). Any equipment
the familiar wears or carries with it is invisible.
```
##### Ability Score Improvement

When you reach 4th level, and again at 8th, 12th, 16th, and 19th level, you can increase
one ability score of your choice by 2, or you can increase two Ability Scores of your
choice by 1. As normal, you can’t increase an ability score above 20 using this feature.

##### Sorcerous Conjuration

Starting at 18th level, you can cast _summon daemon_ , without requiring concentration
and without expending psyker points. Once you use this feature, you can’t use it again
until you complete a long rest.

Additionally, if your total for a Wisdom (Occult) check is less than your psycasting ability
score, you can use that score in place of the total.

##### Master of Sorcery


At 20th level, when casting a psychic power of 5th-level or lower, you can choose to
deal maximum damage with the power, instead of rolling.

Once you use this feature, you can’t use it again until you complete a long rest.

#### Otherworldly Patrons

Otherworldly patrons are the source of your power. You have some garnered power
from such a powerful being, and now that power festers inside of you. You gain features
based on your otherworldly patron that allow you to manifest your powers in unique
ways.

#### Changer of Ways

The Changer of Ways, most often associated with Tzeentch, is a being of powerful
psychic influence that offers its boons in pieces of forbidden knowledge and psychic
power.

##### Forbidden Tome

Starting at 1st level when you choose this patron, you have been granted a tome of
forbidden knowledge, and you determine its appearance when you summon it. You can
perform a ritual over ten minutes to summon this tome if you lose it, and anyone that
isn’t you that attempts to read this tome only reads incomprehensible gibberish. This
tome turns to ash when you die. While this tome is on your person, you can add your
Intelligence modifier to your Occult checks.

Additionally, you can use this tome to empower your psychic powers while it is on your
person. When you cast a psychic power, you can choose to empower it to be cast at one
level higher than you originally casted the power at, and this can exceed the maximum
power level you can cast a power at. You can use this feature a number of times equal
to your proficiency bonus, and you regain all expended uses at the end of a long rest.

##### Awakened Mind

At 1st level, you have been granted the ability to speak telepathically to other creatures.
As a bonus action, you can establish a telepathic link to any creature you can see within
30 feet of you. While this link is established, you and the chosen creature can
telepathically speak to each other with this link. You and the chosen creature do not
need to understand the same language to speak to each other, but you must both speak
at least one language to speak to each other.


This telepathic link lasts for a 1 hour, and can reach out to a range of 1 mile. The link
ends early if you form a connection with another creature, or if you are no longer on the
same plane of existence as the other creature.

##### Warded Mind

At 6th level, your thoughts can't be read by telepathy or other means unless you allow
it. You also have resistance to psionic damage, and you have advantage on saving
throws against being charmed or frightened.

##### Rewrite Fate

Starting at 10th level, you have been granted the ability to rewrite fate. When an ability
check, saving throw, or attack roll is made within 60 feet of you, you can choose to
cause the creature to re-roll the result (no action required), and you can choose which
result they take.

Once you use this feature, you can't use it again until you finish a short or long rest.

##### Crystal Maze

Starting at 14th level, when you hit a creature with an attack, you can use this feature to
instantly transport the target through the endless crystal maze within Tzeentch’s realm.
The creature disappears and hurtles through a nightmare labyrinth for what feels like
years.

At the end of your next turn, the target returns to the space it previously occupied, or
the nearest unoccupied space. If the target is not a daemon of Tzeentch, it takes 10d10
psionic damage as it reels from its horrific experience.

Once you use this feature, you can't use it again until you finish a long rest.

#### Great Unclean One

The Great Unclean One of Nurgle grants its patron the uncanny ability to survive even
near-lethal wounds, and powers of disease and filth.

##### Grandfather’s Embrace

Starting at 1st level when you choose this patron, you gain the embrace of the father of
pestilence. You have resistance to poison damage, you have advantage on saving throws
against being poisoned, and you are immune to all diseases. You cease to age, and
always appear as if you are in your prime.


Additionally, your hit point maximum increases by 1 and increases by 1 again whenever
you gain a level in this class.

##### Absorb Vitality

Also at 1st level, when a creature within 30 feet of you dies, you can use your reaction
to gain temporary hit points equal to your sorcerer level + your psycasting modifier (to a
minimum of 1).

##### Defy Death

Starting at 6th level, when you roll a 16 or higher on a death saving throw, it is treated
as if you rolled a 20 on the d20.

Additionally, when you succeed on a death saving throw, you can choose to regain a
number of hit points equal to your sorcerer level + your psycasting modifier. Once you
use this feature, you can’t use it again until you complete a long rest.

##### Toxic Skin

Starting at 10th level, your blood oozes with toxins. When you take damage from a
melee weapon attack, the attacker takes acid damage equal to your psycasting modifier.

##### Undying Bulwark

Starting at 14th level, you can choose one damage type when you finish a short or long
rest. You gain resistance to that damage type until you choose a different one with this
feature.

#### Eldritch Invocations

##### Armor of Shadows

You can cast _psychic armor_ on yourself at will, without expending psyker points.

##### Ascendant Step

_Prerequisite: 9th level_
You can cast _levitate_ on yourself at will, without expending psyker points.

##### Aspect of the Moon

You no longer need to sleep and can’t be forced to sleep by any means. To gain the


benefits of a long rest, you can spend all 8 hours doing light activity.

##### Beguiling Influence

You gain proficiency in two of the following skills: Deception, Intimidation, Performance
and Persuasion skills.

##### Cloak of Flies

_Prerequisite: 5th level_
As a bonus action, you can surround yourself with a psychic aura that looks like buzzing
flies. The aura extends 5 feet from you in every direction, but not through total cover. It
lasts until you’re incapacitated or you dismiss it as a bonus action.

The aura grants you advantage on Intimidation checks but disadvantage on all other
Charisma checks. Any other creature that starts its turn in the aura takes poison damage
equal to your Charisma modifier (minimum of 0 damage).

Once you use this invocation, you can’t use it again until you finish a short or long rest.

##### Divulgence of Impurity

You gain resistance to radiant damage.

##### Eldritch Sight

You can cast _detect warp_ at will, without expending psyker points.

##### Eyes of the Rune Keeper

You can read all writing.

##### Fiendish Vigor

You can cast _false life_ on yourself at will as a 1st-level power, without expending psyker
points.

##### Gaze of Two Minds

You can use your action to touch a willing humanoid and perceive through its senses
until the end of your next turn. As long as the creature is on the same plane of existence
as you, you can use your action on subsequent turns to maintain this connection,
extending the duration until the end of your next turn. While perceiving through the
other creature’s senses, you benefit from any special senses possessed by that creature,
and you are blinded and deafened to your own surroundings.


##### Ghostly Gaze

_Prerequisite: 7th level_
As an action, you gain the ability to see through solid objects to a range of 30 feet.
Within that range, you have darkvision if you don’t already have it. This special sight
lasts for 1 minute or until your concentration ends (as if you were concentrating on a
power). During that time, you perceive objects as ghostly, transparent images.

Once you use this invocation, you can’t use it again until you finish a short or long rest.

##### Gifts of the Depths

You can breathe underwater, and you gain a swimming speed equal to your walking
speed.

You can also cast _water breathing_ at will, without expending psyker points.

##### Gift of the Ever-Living Ones

_Prerequisite: 3rd level_
Whenever you regain hit points while your familiar is within 100 feet of you, treat any
dice rolled to determine the hit points you regain as having rolled their maximum value
for you.

##### Mask of Many Faces

You can cast _mask of the deceiver_ at will, without expending psyker points.

##### Master of Myriad Forms

_Prerequisite: 15th level_
You can cast _alter self_ at will, without expending psyker points.

##### Misty Visions

You can cast _silent image_ at will, without expending psyker points.

##### One with Shadows

_Prerequisite: 5th level_
When you are in an area of dim light or darkness, you can use your action to become
invisible until you move or take an action or a reaction.


##### Shroud of Shadow

_Prerequisite: 15th level_
You can cast _invisibility_ at will, without expending psyker points.

##### Tomb of Ahriman

_Prerequisite: 5th level_
As a reaction when you take damage, you can entomb yourself in sand, which disperses
at the end of your next turn. You gain 10 temporary hit points per sorcerer level, which
take as much of the triggering damage as possible. Immediately after you take the
damage, your speed is reduced to 0, and you are incapacitated. These effects, including
any remaining temporary hit points, all end when the sand disperses.

Once you use this invocation, you can’t use it again until you finish a short or long rest.

##### Unholy Sight

You can see normally in darkness, even if it is created by enhanced means, to a distance
of 120 feet.

##### Visions of Distant Realms

_Prerequisite: 15th level_
You can cast _arcane eye_ at will, without expending psyker points.

##### Voice of the Chain Master

_Prerequisite: 3rd level_
You can communicate telepathically with your familiar and perceive through your
familiar’s senses as long as you are on the same plane of existence.

Additionally, while perceiving through your familiar’s senses, you can also speak through
your familiar in your own voice, even if your familiar is normally incapable of speech.

##### Waychanger’s Sight

_Prerequisite: 15th level_
You can see the true form of any shapechanger or creature concealed by illusion or
transmutation effects and powers while the creature is within 30 feet of you and within
line of sight.

##### Whispers of the Grave


_Prerequisite: 9th level_
You can cast _speak with dead_ at will, without expending any psyker points.


# Chapter 4: Personality & Background

## Languages

## Imperial Languages

Imperial languages are those present within the Imperium. These languages typically
represent drastically different dialects or ciphers, rather than entirely unique languages.

**_Heretic._** Cultists, mutants, and heretics that have found themselves affiliated with the
Ruinous Powers speak this guttural mixture of slang and Low Gothic to identify
themselves and enemies.
**_High Gothic._** Reserved for nobles and the well-educated, High Gothic is a scholarly
language, and many official and government documents are written in this language. It
is antiquated and proper, with very little slang or derogatory terms within it.
**_Imperial Codes._** Used by many of the armed forces, this language is a cipher used across
the many branches of the Imperium to quickly convey information while also concealing
its true message to any unobservant listener.
**_Low Gothic._** The standard language within the Imperium, almost every human that has
been touched by the Imperium knows this language.
**_Traders’ Cant._** An easy-to-learn cipher system used amongst traders, mercenaries, and
travelers to convey information using common phrases, lingo, and slang.
**_Tribal._** A simple and blunt language found on feudal and feral worlds.
**_Underworld._** From smugglers to chem dealers, Underworld is the language used for
thieves, outlaws, and criminals. It is full of slang, misnomers, and terms used to confuse
or disorient listeners unfamiliar with this language.

```
Language Typical Speakers Script
Heretic Heretics, cultists, mutants Gothic
High Gothic Nobles, space marines,
influential Imperials, wealthy
merchants
```

```

```

#### Exotic Languages

Exotic languages are obscure, alien, or only encountered within a small subset of
people. These languages are typically diverse and rarely found within the Imperium.

**_Aeldari._** The language of the eldar and all of its sub-factions, this is one of the most
complicated languages to know that is full of intricate wordings, phrases, and diverse
body language.
**_Binary._** Spoken by the followers of the Adeptus Mechanicum, this language is also the
same language that most Imperial machinery is programmed in. It consists of zeros and
ones, in both writing and speech.
**_Chaos._** Consisting of enigmatic runes, cryptic phrases, and otherworldly words, Chaos is
the embodiment of the daemons that speak it. Mortals that learn Chaos are usually
intune with the powers of Chaos, but some learn it to better understand and defeat
their foes.
**_Necrontyr._** The ancient language of the Necron, consisting of runes and low drones.
**_Orkish._** A language that consists more of violent gestures and grunts than actual words.
It is brutish, simple, and aggressive.
**_Tau._** The language of the Tau, consisting of light consonants and complex phrases. It is
often spoken with intricate idioms.
**Language Typical Speakers Script**
Aeldari Eldar: craftworld, dark eldar,
and exodite eldar, Sslyth

## Backgrounds

If you are given a proficiency from your background that you have already obtained


from character creation, you can instead choose another skill or tool to gain proficiency.

#### Bounty Hunter

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Insight, Investigation, Perception, and
Stealth
**Tool Proficiencies** : One musical instrument of your choice, security kit
**Equipment** : A set of common clothes, a mark from your last target (such as a lock of
hair, broken dagger, or piece of cloth), and a pouch containing 100 g

##### Feature: Contact Network

You are in frequent contact with people in the segment of society that your chosen
quarries move through. These people might be associated with the criminal underworld,
the rough-and-tumble folk of the streets, or members of high society. This connection
comes in the form of a contact in any civilized planet you visit that has at least one
member of your race on it, a person who provides information about the people and
places of the local area.

#### Chapter Serf

You are the serf of one of the many space marine chapters. Within each chapter is a
diverse and complex system of culture, tradition, and loyalties. As a chapter serf, you
are expected to maintain the equipment and armaments of space marines, provide
basic maintenance for the ships and faculties they use, and in dire circumstances,
defend the chapter’s fortress monastery and vessels while the space marines are not
present.

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Lore, Medicine, Persuasion, and Tech.
**Languages** : One of your choice
**Tool Proficiencies** : One set of artisan’s tools
**Equipment** : A piece of heraldry or emblem of your chapter, a book about your chapter,
a set of serf’s robes (common clothes), a quill, inkpot, parchment, and a pouch
containing 100 g.

##### Serf Training

During your time as a serf, you had a specific role you were given. Roll a d4 or choose
from the options in the table below to determine your training:

```
d4 Serf Training
```

```
1 Artificer - You aided your chapter’s techmarines by repairing and maintaining
equipment, gear and other armaments.
2 Medicae - You assisted the apothecaries and were given medical training.
3 Sacratium - You served alongside the chaplains to tend to the chapter’s relics.
4 Scribellum - The librarians of your chapter trained you to record the histories of the
chapter and create purity seals.
```
##### Feature: Serf Intuition

As a chapter serf, you are well-acquainted with space marines, and the culture and
traditions these battle-brothers share amongst each other. Although you most likely are
not allowed any secrets to your chapter, you are well aware of information such as their
primarch, training schedules, specialities, chapter organization, and general history.
Space marines of this chapter recognize you and your loyalty, and you are able to seek
refuge and shelter from people loyal to this chapter, assuming you do not accost or
endanger them.

#### Charlatan

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Deception, Sleight of Hand, Stealth, and
Performance
**Tool Proficiencies** : Disguise kit, forgery kit
**Equipment** : A set of fine clothes, a disguise kit, tools of the con of your choice (ten
stoppered bottles filled with colored liquid, a set of weighted dice, a deck of marked
cards, or a signet ring of an imaginary duke), and a belt pouch containing 150 g

##### Favorite Schemes

Every Charlatan has an angle they use in preference to other schemes. Choose a favorite
scheme or roll on the table below.

```
d6 Scam
1 I cheat at games of chance.
2 I shave coins or forge documents.
3 I insinuate into people’s lives to prey on their weaknesses and secure their fortunes.
4 I put on new identities like clothes.
5 I run sleight-of-hand cons on street corners.
6 I convince people that worthless junk is worth their hard-earned money.
```
##### Feature: False Identity

You have created a second identity that includes documentation, established
acquaintances, and disguises that allow you to assume that persona. Additionally, you
can forge documents including official papers and personal letters, as long as you have
seen an example of the kind of document or the handwriting you are trying to copy.

#### Criminal

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Deception, Stealth, Intimidation, and Sleight
of Hand
**Tool Proficiencies** : One type of gaming set, security kit
**Equipment** : A crowbar, a set of dark common clothes including a hood, and a belt pouch
containing 150 g

##### Criminal Specialty

There are many kinds of criminals, and within a thieves’ guild or similar criminal


organization, individual members have particular specialities. Even criminals who
operate outside of such organizations have strong preferences for certain kinds of crime
over others. Choose the role you play in your criminal life, or roll on the table below.
.
**d8 Specialty**
1 Blackmailer
2 Burglar
3 Enforcer
4 Fence
5 Highway robber
6 Hired killer
7 Pickpocket
8 Smuggler

##### Feature: Criminal Contact

You have a reliable and trustworthy contact who acts as your liaison to a network of
other criminals. You know how to get messages to and from your contact, even over
great distances; specifically, you know the local messengers, corrupt traders, and seedy
rogue traders who can deliver messages for you.
