#### Diplomat

You have served as a diplomat, negotiating and brokering deals to come to nonviolent
conclusions to benefit both parties. Perhaps you served with the Administratum of the
Imperium to keep the peace between uneasy planets in order for them to continue
producing their tithes, or perhaps you worked as an envoy or ambassador from another
faction, such as the Tau, to bring new planets under the rule as peacefully as possible.

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Deception, Insight, Lore, and Persuasion.
**Languages** : Two of your choice
**Equipment** : A certificate of your office, a set of fine clothes, and a pouch containing 200
g.

##### Feature: Court Process

Your knowledge of how bureaucracies function lets you gain access to the records and
inner workings of any noble court or government you encounter. You know who the
movers and shakers are, whom to go to for the favors you seek, and what the current
intrigues of interest in the group are.

##### Suggested Characterics

```
d6 Personality Trait d6 Ideal
1 I believe that anything worth doing is worth
doing right. I can't help it – I'm a perfectionist.
```
```
1 (Lawful) Community. It is the duty of all
civilized people to strengthen the bonds
community and the security of civilizatio
2 I always want to know how things work and
what makes people tick.
```
```
2 (Good) Generosity. My talents were give
me so that I could use them to benefit th
world.

pursue his or her own livelihood.

#### Disciple

You are a disciple of one of the many religions that dot the galaxy. Whether it be the
Imperial Cult to the Emperor and His many forms, the Machine God, or even the
religions that make up Chaos and the Ruinous Powers, you are a disciple of that religion.
Many disciples that end up as adventurers become exiled or pursue their adventuring
life in pursuit of a holy quest.

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Insight, Lore, Occult, and Medicine.
**Languages** : Two of your choice
**Tool Proficiencies
Equipment** : A holy symbol (of your chosen sect, such as an aquila or chaos star), a
prayer book or prayer wheel, 5 sticks of incense, vestments, a set of common clothes,
and a pouch containing 150 g

##### Feature: Shelter of the Faithful

As an acolyte, you command the respect of those who share your faith, and you can
perform the religious ceremonies related to that of the Imperial Cult. You and your
adventuring companions can expect to receive free healing and care at a temple, shrine,
or other established presence of your faith.Those who share your religion will support


you (but only you) at a modest lifestyle.

#### Entertainer

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Acrobatics, Performance, Persuasion, and
Lore
**Tool Proficiencies:** Disguise kit, one type of musical instrument
**Equipment** : A musical instrument (one of your choice), the favor of an admirer (love
letter, lock of hair, or trinket), costume clothes, and a belt pouch containing 150 g


##### Entertainer Routines

A good entertainer is versatile, spicing up every performance with a variety of different
routines. Choose one to three routines or roll on the table below to define your
expertise as an entertainer.

```
d10 Specialty
1 Actor
2 Dance
3 Fire-eater
4 Jester
5 Juggler
6 Instrumentalist
7 Poet
8 Singer
9 Storyteller
10 Tumbler
```
##### Feature: By Popular Demand

You can always find a place to perform, usually in an inn or tavern but possibly with a
circus, at a theater, or even in a noble's court. At such a place, you receive free lodging
and food of a modest or comfortable standard (depending on the quality of the
establishment), as long as you perform each night. In addition, your performance makes
you something of a local figure. When strangers recognize you in a town where you
have performed, they typically take a liking to you.

#### Heretic

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Deception, Intimidation, Lore, and Occult
**Languages** : Two of your choice
**Equipment** : A set of cultist robes, a set of common clothes, a holy symbol of your
chosen deity, a symbol of your initiation (such as a pickled eye, a finger bone, or a
voodoo doll), and 50 g.

##### Feature: Supine Servitude

As a servant of ill powers, you’ve placated yourself into a position of servitude. You are
familiar with the rituals, aspects, and traits of the deity or philosophy you have
worshipped. Furthermore, you are familiar with the results of said rituals, such as
mutations, boons, banes, and other identifying traits that members of that cult may
have. When seeking refuge, other members of your cult or faith may be able to house
and clothe you, provided you still worship your faith or provide succor for their
ambitions.


#### Mechanic

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Tech, Piloting, Investigation, and Perception
**Tool Proficiencies** : Mechanic’s Kit, Vehicle (one of your choice)
**Equipment** : A wrench, a letter from a customer, a set of common clothes, a mechanic’s
kit, a key to an old vehicle, and a pouch containing 100 g.

##### Feature: Handyman

From a broken toaster to rusted water pipes, people are willing to listen to you for small
mechanical fixes. In exchange for menial labor, people would be willing to provide board
and room for you and your comrades, provided that you have not antagonized them
previously, and are not more trouble than you are worth.

#### Medic

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Lore, Medicine, Nature, and Tech.
**Tool Proficiencies** : Chirurgeon’s Tools
**Equipment** : A vial of chloroform, a stethoscope, a doctor’s bag or suitcase, chirurgeon’s
tools, a trauma kit, common clothes, and a pouch containing 100 g.

##### Feature: Healer of Many

Thanks to your time spent traveling, you are familiar with the regions of the world
enough to know where the skilled healers and surgeons are, as well as where to find the
right medications or materials needed for healing. In a world of few physicians, you can
also easily trade your services. Setting up a clinic or healing tent in town for a few hours
can result in a free meal and roof over your head.

#### Mercenary

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Athletics, Persuasion, Intimidation, and
Acrobatics
**Tool Proficiencies:** One type of gaming set, vehicles (land)
**Equipment** : A uniform of your company (traveler's clothes in quality), an insignia of your
rank, a gaming set of your choice, and a pouch containing the remainder of your last
wages (100 g).

##### Feature: Mercenary Life


You know the mercenary life as only someone who has experienced it can. You are able
to identify mercenary companies by their emblems, and you know a little about any
such company, including who may have hired them recently. You can find the taverns
and festhalls where mercenaries abide in any area, as long as you speak the language.

#### Military

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Athletics, Intimidation, Perception, and
Medicine
**Tool Proficiencies** : One type of gaming set, vehicles (land)
**Equipment** : An insignia of rank, a trophy taken from a fallen enemy (a dagger, broken
blade, or piece of a banner), a dice set or playing card set, a set of common clothes, and
a belt pouch containing 100 g

##### Feature: Military Rank

You have a military rank from your career. Forces loyal to your former military
organization still recognize your authority and influence, and they defer to you if they
are of a lower rank. You can invoke your rank to exert influence over other soldiers and
requisition simple equipment or horses for temporary use. You can also usually gain
access to friendly military encampments and fortresses where your rank is recognized.

#### Noble

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Lore, Persuasion, Deception, and
Performance
**Tool Proficiencies** : One type of gaming set
**Languages** : One of your choice
**Equipment** : A set of fine clothes, a signet ring, a scroll of pedigree, and a purse
containing 250 g

##### Feature: Position of Privilege

Thanks to your noble birth, people are inclined to think the best of you. You are
welcome in high society, and people assume you have the right to be wherever you are.
The common folk make every effort to accommodate you and avoid your displeasure,
and other people of high birth treat you as a member of the same social sphere. You can
secure an audience with a local noble if you need to.

#### Outlander

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Athletics, Survival, Nature, and Perception
**Tool Proficiencies** : One type of musical instrument

**Equipment** : A staff, a hunting trap, a trophy from an animal you killed, a set of traveler's
clothes, and a belt pouch containing 100 g

##### Origin

You’ve been to strange places and seen things that others cannot begin to fathom.

you. You may determine your occupation during your time in the wild, or roll on the

##### Feature: Wanderer

You have an excellent memory for maps and geography, and you can always recall the
general layout of terrain, settlements, and other features around you. In addition, you
can find food and fresh water for yourself and up to five other people each day,
provided that the land offers berries, small game, water, and so forth.

#### Pilgrim

You lived as a travelling pilgrim, going from holy sites across the galaxy in the name of
your faith. Along the pilgrim routes, you may have seen a fair amount of the galaxy,
from its wondrous cities of golden skyscrapers that touch the clouds, to planets that
amount to little more than barren deserts of rock and dust.

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Lore, Occult, Performance, and Persuasion
**Languages** : Two of your choice
**Equipment** : A set of traveler’s clothes, and a pouch containing 50 g.

##### Feature: Holy Shrines

Shrines are dotted across the galaxy, with the routes pilgrims usually take well known.
As a pilgrim, you are familiar with these shrines dedicated to your faith, as well as basic
information such as how well-patrolled they are, if raiders or pirates inhabit that
airspace, and the general history behind these shrines.

#### Pilot

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Piloting, Perception, Performance, and Tech
**Tool Proficiencies** : Vehicles (all)
**Equipment** : A fancy key fob to a vehicle, a magazine about vehicles, a pair of fuzzy dice,
a set of traveler’s clothes, and 100 g

##### Feature: Vehicle Expert

In your time as a pilot, you’ve learned to identify any and all vehicles on the road. From
basic-model bicycles to high-tech star cruisers, you’re familiar with at least the basic
functions and features of most vehicles. If something is so exotic that you have not seen
it before, you can often pinpoint an origin or similarities the vehicle has to others you
may have seen.

#### Police Force

You were a part of a city’s police force, such as an arbitrator, or a planetary defense
force. You have served to protect the collective interests of the planet. Perhaps you
disagreed with some of the regulations on your home world, or perhaps you were an
ardent enforcer of the law, regardless of circumstance. Think about how your world
dealt with crime and the issues that plague the galaxy, and if your planet ever
experienced attacks or raids from outside forces.


**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Athletics, Intimidation, Investigation, and
Perception.
**Languages** : One of your choice
**Tool Proficiencies** : Vehicles (land)
**Equipment** : A uniform (fine clothes), a police baton (club), a whistle, a set of manacles, a
letter from a coworker about a case that went cold, and a pouch containing 100 g.

##### Feature: Police Rank

As a member of the police force, you have a badge of your office that displays your
authority. Using this, you can enter areas that might have been previously restricted and
access a modicum of their records based on your rank, such as local police records,
surveillance footage, and locals are more likely to trust you, unless you or your position
has a negative reputation.

#### Preserved

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Lore, Investigation, Occult, and Insight.
**Tool Proficiencies** : One gaming set or musical instrument of your choice
**Equipment** : A book that was preserved with you, a small hourglass, a set of dated
common clothes, and a pouch containing 100 g.

##### Feature: Knowledge of the Ages

You are a relic of a different time—whether through cryogenic stasis, time travel, or
warp phenomena, you are from a time hundreds, if not thousands, of years in the past.
You can accurately recall any information from your time period, warranted that the
information was either common knowledge or involved you directly.

#### Raider

Within the galaxy, many species resort to raiding and pillaging. Whether it be the
common pirate, a brigand looking for his next meal, or an entire regiment gone rogue,
these raiders are found throughout the galaxy, in times of peace and war, and lead lives
of difficulty and strife in exchange for their self-perceived freedom.

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Acrobatics, Athletics, Perception, Piloting
**Tool Proficiencies** : Security kit, navigator's tools, vehicles (land or space)
**Equipment** : A trophy taken from a raid such as a broken dagger or torn banner, a set of
common clothes, and a pouch containing 50 g.

##### Feature: Bad Reputation

No matter where you go, people are afraid of you due to your reputation. When you are
in a civilized settlement, you can get away with minor criminal offenses, such as refusing
to pay for food at a bar or breaking down doors at a local shop, since most people will
not report your activity to the authorities.

#### Rogue Trader

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Lore, Piloting, Investigation, and Tech
**Languages** : One of your choice
**Tool Proficiencies** : Vehicles (one of your choice), navigator’s tools
**Equipment** : A memento from your previous ship, a set of common clothes, and 100 g,
and a starchart of your most frequented routes.

##### Feature: Starfinder

You have an excellent memory for star charts and constellations, and you can always
recall the general layout of star systems, space stations, and planets that you have been
to or have studied. In addition, you know the most popular routes taken by rogue


traders.

#### Sailor

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Athletics, Perception, Nature, and Sleight of
Hand
**Tool Proficiencies** : Navigator's tools, vehicles (water) or vehicles (space)
**Equipment** : A belaying pin (club), silk rope (50 feet), a lucky charm such as a rabbit foot
or a small stone with a hole in the center (or you may roll for a random trinket on the
Trinkets table in chapter 5), a set of common clothes, and a belt pouch containing 100 g

##### Feature: Ship’s Passage

When you need to, you can secure free passage on a ship for yourself and your
adventuring companions. You might sail on the ship you served on, or another ship you
have good relations with (perhaps one captained by a former crewmate). Because
you're calling in a favor, you can't be certain of a schedule or route that will meet your
every need. Your DM will determine how long it takes to get where you need to go. In
return for your free passage, you and your companions are expected to assist the crew
during the voyage.

#### Scavenger

Amongst the sprawling hive cities to the humblest of scrap yards, scavengers make their
living picking apart through the heaps and wreckages of littered technology to survive.
Some scavengers might come across a lively profession, joining a crew with a scavenging
ship dedicated to picking apart the wreckages of old battlefields in space or planet
hopping until they find valuable salvage.

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Investigation, Lore, Sleight of Hand, and
Stealth.
**Tool Proficiencies** : Mechanic’s kit, one of your choice
**Equipment** : An unknown piece of heraldry, a broken weapon, and a unique piece of
minted currency, a set of traveler’s clothes, and a pouch containing 100 g.

##### Feature: Salvage

You know the best places to scavenge, and can make rudimentary gear out of the items
you scavenge. When you are in a civilized or urban area, you can spend several hours
scavenging around for scrap and junk in order to make an item that can be found under
Adventuring Gear found within Chapter 5: Standard Equipment, as long as the price is
100 g or less. This item is considered as near-useless to most merchants and vendors,
making it unable to be sold.

#### Scholar

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Lore, Occult, Investigation, and Nature
**Languages** : Two of your choice
**Equipment** : A bottle of black ink, a quill, a small knife, a letter from a dead colleague
posing a question you have not yet been able to answer, a set of common clothes, and a
belt pouch containing 100 g

##### Feature: Researcher

When you attempt to learn or recall a piece of lore, if you do not know that information,
you often know where and from whom you can obtain it. Usually, this information
comes from a library, scriptorium, university, or a sage or other learned person or
creature. Your DM might rule that the knowledge you seek is secreted away in an
almost inaccessible place, or that it simply cannot be found. Unearthing the deepest
secrets of the multiverse can require an adventure or even a whole campaign.


#### Slave

You were taken as a slave or an indentured servant. Whether you were asked to
perform menial tasks as a waiter, or forced to fight in a slave-army for a wealthy
governor, you share some things in common with other slaves of the same ilk.

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Athletics, Acrobatics, Deception, and
Survival.
**Tool Proficiencies** : Two tools of your choice
**Equipment** : A set of traveler’s clothes, a pendant of a friend that is still enslaved, a
token from your previous owner such as an emblem, watch, or badge, and a pouch
containing 10 g.

##### Feature: Downtrodden Comradery

Within the greater galaxy, the need for labor is strong. From the common factory
worker to the humblest of slave-gladiators, you can find a friend in these folks. Using
these connections, you can find information about current politics from these slaves,
information about their masters, as well as what kind of work they do.

#### Smuggler

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Athletics, Deception, Piloting, and
Investigation
**Tool Proficiencies** : Vehicles (one of your choice)
**Equipment** : A fancy leather vest or a pair of leather boots, a set of common clothes, and
a leather pouch with 150 g

##### Feature: Down Low

You are acquainted with a network of smugglers who are willing to help you out of tight
situations. While in a particular town, city, or other similarly sized community (DM's
discretion), you and your companions can stay for free in safe houses. Safe houses
provide a poor lifestyle. While staying at a safe house, you can choose to keep your
presence (and that of your companions) a secret.

#### Tech Priest

Within the Cult of the Machine God, the common members are known simply as tech
priests. These priests believe that true enlightenment comes from replacing the weak
flesh of the human body with the immortal structure of machines. Venerable members
of the Machine Cult may have only a few organs remaining that represent their original
human forms, while many become unrecognizable mixtures of machine and man shortly
after their initiation.

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Lore, Medicine, Piloting, and Tech.
**Languages** : One of your choice
**Tool Proficiencies** : One tech gadget of your choice
**Equipment** : A symbol of the Mechanicum cog, a set of red robes of the Machine Cult
(fine clothes), a small piece of unknown technology such as a broken watch or stagnant


cogitator, and a pouch containing 100 g.

##### Feature: Machine Cult Implants

You have cybernetic implants from the Machine Cult, allowing you to attune to the
machine spirits of technology more easily. When interacting with a piece of technology,
such as a weapon, machine, or vehicle, you are able to communicate with its machine
spirit. You can learn how old the piece of technology is, the mood of the machine spirits,
as well as if it has been consecrated or desecrated. You may also learn other features
about the piece of technology at the GM’s discretion, depending on the intelligence of
the machine spirit. For example, a land raider may have more knowledge extending to
the battles it’s fought in, while a measly lasgun might only know how many times it’s
been fired in the past day.

#### Urchin

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Sleight of Hand, Deception, Insight, and
Perception
**Tool Proficiencies** : Disguise kit, Security Kit
**Equipment** : A small knife, a map of the city you grew up in, a pet mouse, a token to
remember your parents by, a set of common clothes, and a belt pouch containing 100 g

##### Feature: City Secrets

You know the secret patterns and flow to cities and can find passages through the urban
sprawl that others would miss. When you are not in combat, you (and companions you
lead) can travel between any two locations in the city twice as fast as your speed would
normally allow.

#### Witchhunter

**Skill Proficiencies** : Choose two from among Occult, Insight, Lore, and Investigation
**Tool Proficiencies** : Poisoner’s Kit
**Languages** : One of your choice
**Equipment** : A trophy from a mark (such as a lock of hair, a wanted poster, or a feather),
a trinket to ward off evil (such as a dream-catcher, cloves of garlic, or a silver chain), a
set of traveler’s clothes, and a pouch containing 50 g.

##### Feature: Scourge of the Damned

When investigating sources of evil, you are familiar with the common deities, gods,
patrons, and sources from which evil originates. Even if you are not able to determine
an exact source from unnatural or otherworldly effects, you can often associate it with a
specific deity or group.


# Chapter 5: Standard Equipment

If you are looking for enhanced items like bolt weapons, click HERE.

## Starting Equipment

When you create your character, you receive equipment based on a combination of
your class and background. Alternatively, you can start with an amount of gelt based on
your class and spend them on items from the lists in this section. See the Starting
Wealth by Class table to determine how much gold you have to spend.

You decide how your character came by this starting equipment. It might have been an
inheritance, or goods that the character purchased during his or her upbringing. You
might have been equipped with a weapon, armor, and a backpack as part of military
service. You might even have stolen your gear. A weapon could be a family heirloom,
passed down from generation to generation until your character finally took up the
mantle and followed in an ancestor’s adventurous footsteps.

```
Class Augmenticist Berserker Courser Crusader
Funds 2d4 x 100 g 2d4 x 100 g 5d4 x 100 g 5d4 x 100 g
Class Exorcist Mechnician Psyker Renegade
Funds 5d4 x 100 g 4d4 x 100 g 5d4 x 100 g 4d4 x 100 g
Class Soldier Sorcerer
Funds 5d4 x 100 g 3d4 x 100 g
```
## Wealth

Wealth appears in many forms in the galaxy. Coins, gemstones, trade goods, art objects,
animals, and property can reflect your character’s financial well-being. Members of the
lower class trade in goods, bartering for what they need and paying tithes in grain and
cheese.

Members of the nobility trade either in legal rights, such as the rights to a mine, a port,
or farmland, or in gold bars or gemstones, measuring gold and gems by the pound
rather than by the coin. Only merchants, adventurers, and those offering professional
services for hire commonly deal in coins.

## Wealth Conversion Rates


Coinage has been converted into throne gelt, or gelt for short. The conversion rate is 1
sp = 1 Gelt. 10 gelt is equal to 1 gold, and so forth. If something is worth 100 gold,
multiply it by 10 to get its value in gelt. If the adventure is taking place in a non-Imperial
setting, the currency can change. For example, instead of gelt, you can use ork teeth.

#### Selling Treasure

Opportunities abound to find treasure, equipment, weapons, armor, and more in the
worlds you explore. Normally, you can sell your treasures and trinkets when you return
to a town or other settlement, provided that you can find buyers and merchants
interested in your loot.

##### Arms, Armor, and Other Equipment

As a general rule, undamaged weapons, armor, and other equipment fetch half their
cost when sold in a market. Weapons and armor used by monsters are rarely in good
enough condition to sell.

##### Enhanced Items

Selling advanced technology is problematic. Finding someone to buy a vial of toxins or a
medpac isn't too hard, but other items are out of the realm of most but the wealthiest
nobles. Likewise, aside from a few common enhanced items, you won't normally come
across enhanced items or powers to purchase. The value of rare technology is far
beyond simple gelt and should always be treated as such.

##### Gems, Jewelry, and Art Objects

These items retain their full value in the marketplace, and you can either trade them in
for currency or use them as currency for other transactions. For exceptionally valuable
treasures, the DM might require you to find a buyer in a large town or larger community
first.

##### Trade Goods and Other

On the borderlands, many people conduct transactions through barter. Like gems and
art objects, trade goods--bars of iron, bags of salt, livestock, and so on--retain their full
value in the market and can be used as currency.

## Armor and Shields


##### Armor Class

Armor protects its wearer from attacks. The armor (and shield) you wear determines
your armor class (AC).

##### Armor Properties

**_Bulky._** While wearing armor with the bulky property, you have disadvantage on
Dexterity (Stealth) checks that rely on sound.
**_Strength._** While wearing armor or wielding a shield with the strength property, your
speed is reduced by 10 unless you meet the strength requirement.
**_Sealed._** While wearing this armor, you can breathe normally underwater and in toxic
environments, such as miasma and poisonous atmospheres, and you do not suffer
harmful effects from being in dangerous climates, such as deep underwater, high
altitude, heat, cold, radiation, or in a vacuum.

##### Light Armor

**_Mesh armor._** Often used by poorly equipped militiamen or thugs, the breastplate
and shoulder protectors of this armor are made of mesh that has been stiffened to
allow freedom of movement around joints whilst guarding the more vulnerable parts of
the body.
**_Fiber armor._** Made from tough fiber, interwoven into thin sheets, this armor
provides protection against blows while still allowing the wearer to not be encumbered
by armor.
**_Bodyglove._** This suit is made from cloisters of fibers that have been woven to form
an environmental seal at the cost of stealth, and are often found in the hands of
explorators and rogue traders.

##### Medium Armor

**_Chain mail._** Made of interlocking metal rings, chain mail includes a layer of quilted
fabric worn underneath the mail to prevent chafing and to cushion the impact of blows.
This is most commonly found on Feudal Worlds and within exceptionally poor fighting
forces.
**_Flak armor._** Commonly found amongst the soldiers of the Imperial Guard, this armor
is reinforced against ballistics and explosives, while still allowing a modicum of
movement to not restrict mobility.
**_Trooper armor._** Made of densely layered plates of armaplas, ceramite, or other
hardy materials, this armor has been modified to remove the armor around the
wearer’s joints to allow some freedom of movement. This armor is used by local
planetary defense forces and arbitrator patrols.


**_Composite armor._** Interlocking plates of carapace come together to form a layer of
protective coverings over the chest, shoulders, and thighs. This is issued to some officers
in the Imperial Guard and used by wealthy mercenaries.
**_Light power armor._** Thin plates of ceramite and armaplas are bolted onto a suit of
interwoven fibers and metal to provide a lightweight frame that allows a degree of
flexibility, as opposed to standard power armor. This is commonly used amongst elite
fighting forces, such as Sisters of Battle and high-ranking members of the Imperial
Guard.

##### Heavy Armor

**_Feudal plate._** Traditional plate armor typically found on Feudal Worlds made of
plates of steel or iron.
**_Battle armor._** Armor that restricts movement, but covers the wearer’s body and
joints in protective plates melded together to form a protective sheet over the majority
of the wearer’s body. This is often rewarded to a survivor of a few battles, and is often
found in the hands of veterans and officers.
**_Combat suit._** Thick plates made of ceramite or armaplas come together to create a
suit that encloses the wearer in its form. This is often used by shock troopers that have
survived many battles.
**_Power armor._** Ceramite plates are plastered onto a suit of interwoven fibers and
metals, and powered by an indefinite source of power, such as a plasma or nuclear
reactor, with a full seal that protects the user from the environment. Typically found in
the hands of Space Marines or Inquisitors, this armor is a mark of prestige and power.

##### Shields

**_Shield._** A shield is a round or rectangular barrier used to place something between
yourself and your attacker. Commonly found shields include riot shields, planks of wood,
or sheets of metal.

## Weapon Properties

**_Ammunition._** You can use a weapon that has the ammunition property to make a
ranged attack only if you have ammunition to fire from the weapon. Each time you
attack with the weapon, you expend one piece of ammunition. If you use a weapon that
has the ammunition property to make a melee attack, you treat the weapon as an
improvised weapon.
**_Finesse._** When making an attack with a finesse weapon, you use your choice of your
Strength or Dexterity modifier for the attack and damage rolls. You must use the same
modifier for both rolls.
**_Light._** A light weapon is small and easy to handle, making it ideal for use when
fighting with two weapons. See the rules for two-weapon fighting in chapter 9.
**_Range._** A weapon that can be used to make a ranged attack has a range shown in
parentheses after the ammunition or thrown property. The range lists two numbers.
The first is the weapon’s normal range in feet, and the second indicates the weapon’s
maximum range. When attacking a target beyond normal range, you have disadvantage
on the attack roll. You can’t attack a target beyond the weapon’s long range.
**_Reach._** This weapon adds 5 feet to your reach with it.
**_Loading._** Because of the time required to load this weapon, you can fire only one
piece of ammunition from it when you use an action, bonus action, or reaction to fire it,
regardless of the number of attacks you can normally make.
**_Reload._** A limited number of shots can be made with a weapon that has the reload
property. A character must then reload it (no action required). You must have one free
hand to reload.
**_Special._** A weapon with the special property has unusual rules governing its use,
explained in the weapon’s description (see “Special Weapons” later in this section).


**_Strength._** A weapon with this special property has a heavy kickback. While wielding
it, you have disadvantage on attack rolls using that weapon unless you meet the
Strength requirement.
**_Thrown._** If a weapon has the thrown property, you can throw the weapon to make a
ranged attack. If the weapon is a melee weapon, you use the same ability modifier for
that attack roll and damage roll that you would use for a melee attack with the weapon.
**_Two-Handed._** This weapon requires two hands to use.
**_Versatile._** This weapon can be used with one or two hands. A damage value in
parentheses appears with the property-the damage when the weapon is used with two
hands to make a melee attack.

#### Special Weapons

**_Net_**_._ A Large or smaller creature hit by a net is restrained until it is freed. A net has
no effect on formless or Huge or larger creatures. A creature can use its action to make
a DC 13 Strength check, freeing itself or another creature within its reach on a success.
The net has an AC of 10, 5 hit points, and immunity to all damage not dealt by melee
weapons. Destroying the net frees the creature without harming it and immediately
ends the net’s effects. While a creature is restrained by a net, you can make no further
attacks with it.
**_Flamer_**_._ Instead of choosing a target to attack, the flamer shoots out a gout of flame in a
10-foot line that is 5 feet wide. You make attack rolls against the creatures within the
line of flame, and on a successful hit, the target takes damage from the flamer. Flamers
use promethium as ammunition.

#### Improvised Weapons

Sometimes characters don't have their weapons and have to attack with whatever is at
hand. An improvised weapon includes any object you can wield in one or two hands,
such as broken glass, a table leg, a frying pan, a wagon wheel, or a dead snotling.

Often, an improvised weapon is similar to an actual weapon and can be treated as such.
For example, a table leg is akin to a club. At the DM's option, a character proficient with
a weapon can use a similar object as if it were that weapon and use his or her
proficiency bonus.

An object that bears no resemblance to a weapon deals 1d4 damage (the DM assigns a
damage type appropriate to the object). If a character uses a ranged weapon to make a
melee attack, or throws a melee weapon that does not have the thrown property, it also
deals 1d4 damage. An improvised thrown weapon has a normal range of 20 feet and a
long range of 60 feet.


#### Blessed Weapons

Some monsters that have immunity or resistance to nonenhanced weapons are
susceptible to blessed weapons, so cautious witchhunters invest extra gelt to bless their
weapons. You can bless a single weapon or ten pieces of ammunition for 1,000 gelt. This
cost represents not only the price of the holy ointments and unguents, but the time and
expertise needed to bless the weapon with the proper rites and ceremonies.

Handgun 350 g 1d8 kinetic 2 lbs. Ammunition (range 40/160), reload 6
Net 10 g — 2 lbs. Special, thrown (range 5/15)
Pistol 280 g 1d6 kinetic 2 lbs. Ammunition (range 40/160), light, reload 6
Sniper rifle 475 g 1d12 kinetic 8 lbs. Ammunition (range 150/600), loading, reload 4
handed
Assault rifle 375 g 1d10 kinetic 6 lbs. Ammunition (range 100/400), reload 12, two-h
Combat shotgun 380 g 1d12 kinetic 6 lbs. Ammunition (range 30/120), reload 4, two-han
```

## Adventuring Gear

#### Equipment Packs

The starting equipment you get from your class includes a collection of useful
adventuring gear, put together in a pack. The contents of these packs are listed here. If
you are buying your starting equipment, you can purchase a pack for the price shown,
which might be cheaper than buying the items individually.

##### Burglar’s Pack

Costs 290 gelt. Includes a backpack, a glow lamp with two power cells, 1,000 ball
bearings, a crowbar, a chrono, a lighter, a grappling hook, a commlink, 5 days of field
rations, and a canteen.

##### Diplomat’s Pack

Costs 530 gelt. Includes a chest, 2 cases for maps and scrolls, a bottle of ink and an ink
pen, a commlink, sealing wax, soap, a vial of perfume, a set of fine clothes, a data slate,
5 days of field rations, and a canteen.

##### Dungeoneer’s Pack

Costs 320 gelt. Includes a backpack, a glow lamp with five power cells, a crowbar, a
hammer, a commlink, a grappling hook, a chrono, 10 days of field rations, a canteen,
and 50 feet of hempen rope strapped to the side of it.

##### Entertainer’s Pack

Costs 420 gelt. Includes a backpack, a bedroll, two costumes, a glow lamp with two
power cells, 5 days of field rations, a canteen, a commlink, and a disguise kit.

##### Explorer’s Pack

Costs 250 gelt. Includes a backpack, a bedroll, a blanket, a mess kit, a glow lamp with
two power cells, 10 days of field rations, a canteen, a commlink, and 50 feet of hempen
rope strapped to the side of it.

##### Priest’s Pack

Costs 275 gelt. Includes a backpack, a blanket, a glow lamp with two power cells, a data
slate, a trauma kit, a commlink, 5 days of field rations, and a canteen.


##### Scholar’s Pack

Costs 290 gelt. Includes a backpack, a data slate, a commlink, 2 scrolls, a bottle of ink
and a quill, 5 days of field rations, and a canteen.

##### Technologist’s Pack

Costs 670 gelt. Includes a backpack, chrono, respirator, data slate, commlink, bedroll,
canteen, and 5 days of field rations

#### Ammunition

Ammunition comes in many forms, but is most often found in the form of magazines or
cartridges. A magazine or cartridge is a way to store ammunition, such as bullets or bolts
shells. One magazine or cartridge carries all of the ammunition a ranged weapon
requires before needing to be reloaded. At the GM’s discretion, exotic ammunition
(such as plasma cartridges) may be too difficult to find in certain locations, may require
additional efforts to be found, or be purchased at a higher cost.

```
Item Cost Weight
Ammunition
Ammo Bag 250 g 5 lbs.
Dart 1 g —
Magazine 10 g —
Power Cell 10 g —
Promethium, 1 quart 50 g 1 lbs.
```
##### Ammo Bag

An ammo bag is a leather pouch that can be fitted to a backpack or waist that has
compartments to hold all of the ammunition used for weapons. While an ammo bag is
on your person, you are always considered as having ammunition available to reload a
weapon, unless a weapon specifies it needs a special type of ammunition (such as
mortar shells or grenades).

##### Dart

These are darts used as throwing projectiles. They are less than a foot long in length,
and typically made of wood or metal and sharpened to a point.

##### Magazine


This is used to supply ammunition for weapons that deal kinetic damage. One magazine
has all of the ammunition needed until a weapon needs to be reloaded.

##### Power Cell

A power cell is used to power small electrical objects or as ammunition for weapons.
One power cell provides enough ammunition for a weapon that deals energy damage
until it needs to be reloaded. Power cells can also be used to fuel enhanced weapons
that do not deal kinetic damage, such as plasma weapons.

##### Promethium

Promethium is a combustible, gasoline-like liquid that is used to fuel most vehicles and
some forms of weaponry, such as flamers. It is most often found within the Imperium of

Man, but some other factions use it due to its simplicity and versatility.

#### Communications

```
Item Cost Weight
Communications
Commlink 50 g —
Comm Jammer 450 g 1 lbs.
Long-range Comm 250 g 5 lbs.
Comm Tracker 100 g 1 lbs.
Pocket Scrambler 800 g —
Headcomm 100 g —
```
#### Commlink

Commlinks are standard handheld communication devices, fitted with microphones and
receivers. A standard, personal commlinks have a range of up to 30 miles, but are
reduced in dense, urban areas or areas of high level interference.

##### Comm Jammer

A comm jammer is a device used to scramble communications. A comm jammer can
block transmissions from nonenhanced communications devices in a 100 foot radius.

##### Long-range Comm

Long-range comms usually come in the form of voxcasters: bulky radios that require a
steady supply of power. When used, a long-range comm is able to transmit and receive


messages up to thousands of miles away, such as from planetside to an orbiting
satellite. Due to the nature of such a device, encryption is very difficult, if not
impossible.

##### Comm Tracker

As an action, you can use this to detect other active commlinks within 30 feet. When
used in this way, it briefly disrupts comm frequencies.

##### Pocket Scrambler

A pocket scrambler is a simple add-on to any commlink that automatically encodes any
messages sent out. The transmitted message can only be read by a device equipped
with a matched scrambler that can decode the message.

##### Headcomm

A headcomm can be installed in a helmet or worn independently. It functions as a
hands-free commlink.

#### Data Recording & Storage

```
Item Cost Weight
Data Recording & Storage
Data Slate 50 g 2 lbs.
Pict Recorder 150 g 3 lbs.
Voice Recorder 75 g 1 lbs.
```
##### Data Slate

Data slates are common across the universe, and are the primary means of storing and
reading printed text and other forms of data such as picts of audio recordings.

##### Pict Recorder

The pict recorder is a rectangular object with a lens on the front used to capture
pictures, motion pictures, and audio. A pict recorder can be placed inside of a servo skull
for constant recording duties. The information stored on a Pict Recorder can be
uploaded to data slates and other recording devices.

##### Voice Recorder

A voice recorder is a small device that can be hidden under clothes or armor and can
capture audio. This device must be connected to a data slate or similar storage device in


order to store the information.

#### Explosives

```
Item Cost Weight
Explosives
Breaching Charge 750 g 4 lbs.
Explosive Collar 500 g 3 lbs.
Grenade, Stun 250 g 1 lbs.
Grenade, Fragmentation 100 g 1 lbs.
Grenade, Gas 300 g 1 lbs.
Grenade, Haywire 250 g 1 lbs.
Mine, Fragmentation 500 g 2 lbs.
Mine, Thermal 550 g 2 lbs.
Thermal Detonator 750 g 1 lbs.
```
##### Breaching Charge

A device used to blow holes in larger constructs, a breaching charge creates a
devastating explosion. Installing a breaching charge takes 1 minute. The charge can be
set with a 6-second timer, or detonated remotely using a remote detonator.

Once detonated, the breaching charge destroys an nonenhanced section of wall up to
10 feet wide, 10 feet tall, and 5 feet deep. Additionally, each creature within 20 feet of
the charge must make a DC 13 Dexterity saving throw. A creature takes 3d6 fire damage
and 3d6 kinetic damage on a failed save, or half as much on a successful one. A
construct makes this save with disadvantage. If the breaching charge is installed on the
construct, it automatically fails the saving throw.

##### Explosive Collar

Explosive collars are devices that are fitted onto the necks of creatures to ensure
humanoids. The collar requires one minute to install onto a creature of Large or smaller
size, and is connected to a remote that can be activated from up to 120 feet away.
When activated, the collar explodes in a 5 foot radius, and any creatures inside of the
radius must make a DC 11 Constitution saving throw, taking 3d6 fire damage plus 3d6
kinetic damage on a failure, and half as much on a success. Once detonated, the collar is
destroyed and turned into an unusable husk. As an action, the collar can be removed by
a DC 11 Intelligence (Tech) skill check, or by a DC 11 Dexterity skill check using a security
kit. If the skill check fails, the explosive detonates. On a success, the collar is removed
without incident, and the explosives can be disarmed as part of removing the collar.


##### Grenade, Stun

Stun grenades are usually used when the object of a mission is to detain, capture, or
subdue rather than kill. Grenades can be thrown up to 60 feet. As an action, you can
throw a grenade at a point you can see within range. Each creature within 10 feet must
make a DC 12 Dexterity saving throw. A creature takes 1d6 lightning damage on a failed
save, or half as much as on a successful one. Additionally, on a failed save, the creature
is stunned until the end of its next turn.

##### Grenade, Fragmentation

Frag grenades are cheap, low-damage grenades used mainly by military personnel,
mercenaries, bounty hunters, and adventurers. Grenades can be set to detonate on
impact or set with a timer that lasts several seconds before detonating. Grenades can be
thrown up to 60 feet. As an action, you can throw a grenade at a point you can see
within range. Each creature within 10 feet must make a DC 12 Dexterity saving throw. A
creature takes 2d6 kinetic damage on a failed save, or half as much as on a successful
one.

##### Grenade, Gas

Gas grenades are primarily used to flush enemies out of cover and other protected
areas, though there are of course other uses. Grenades can be thrown up to 60 feet. As
an action, you can throw a grenade at a point you can see within range. The grenade
explodes in a 15-foot-radius sphere of yellow-green fog centered on a point you choose
within range. The sphere spreads around corners, and its area is heavily obscured. It
lasts for 1 minute or until a wind of at least 10 miles per hour disperses it.

When a creature enters the fog’s area for the first time on a turn or starts its turn there,
that creature must make a DC 12 Constitution saving throw. The creature takes 1d6
poison damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one.
Additionally, on a failed save, the creature is poisoned while it is in the cloud. Constructs
and humanoids wearing appropriate protective equipment are unaffected.

##### Grenade, Haywire

Haywire grenades are hand-held explosive devices that release a blast of electric
energy. Grenades can be thrown up to 60 feet. As an action, you can throw a grenade at
a point you can see within range. Each creature within 10 feet must make a DC 12
Dexterity saving throw. A creature takes 2d4 lightning damage on a failed save, or half
as much as on a successful one. Any nonenhanced electronics that are not being worn
or wielded within the blast radius are disabled until rebooted.


##### Mine, Fragmentation

When you use your action to set it, this mine sets an imperceptible laser line extending
up to 15 feet. When the laser is tripped, the mine explodes, and each creature within 15
feet of it must make a DC 12 Dexterity saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes
3d6 kinetic damage, or half as much on a successful one.

##### Mine, Thermal

When you use your action to set it, this mine sets an imperceptible laser line extending
up to 15 feet. When the laser is tripped, the mine explodes, coating the area in a 15-foot
radius around it in fire that burns for 1 minute. When a creature enters the fire or starts
its turn there it must make a DC 12 Dexterity saving throw. On a failed save, the
creature takes 2d6 fire damage, or half as much on a successful one. A construct makes
this save with disadvantage.

##### Thermal Detonator

Thermal detonators are palm-sized, spherical, and extremely deadly explosive weapons.
In addition to being surprisingly powerful for their size, they can only be turned off by
whoever turned them on. Thermal detonators have a range equal to 30 feet + your
Strength modifier x 5. As an action, you can throw a thermal detonator at a point you
can see within range. Each creature within 10 feet must make a DC 12 Dexterity saving
throw. A creature takes 2d6 fire and 2d6 kinetic damage on a failed save, or half as
much as on a successful one. Additionally, on a failed save, the creature is knocked
prone.

#### Life Support

```
Item Cost Weight
Life Support
Aquatic rebreather 100 g 2 lbs.
Enviro-suit 2,000 g 15 lbs.
Flight suit 1,000 g 5 lbs.
Respirator 200 g 1 lbs.
```
##### Aquatic Rebreather

Aquatic breathers are breath masks designed to operate underwater. While worn, the
wearer can breathe both air and water.


##### Enviro-suit

Environment suits are pressure suits that enable wearers to survive and operate in zero
gravity space and other dangerous conditions and comes with a built-in rebreather.
While wearing this, you can breathe normally underwater and in toxic environments,
such as miasma and poisonous gas, and you do not suffer harmful effects from being in
dangerous climates, such as deep underwater, high altitude, heat, cold, radiation, or
vacuums.

##### Flight Suit

Flight suits, or jumpsuits, are a type of outfit worn by pilots. They are worn in
conjunction with flight helmets. They come in a variety of different colors and provide
life support.

While wearing a full flight suit, you can last twice as long before suffering negative
effects when exposed to the effects of a vacuum, environmental radiation, and
environmental effects such as the extremes of heat and cold, and high and low
altitudes. Furthermore, you have advantage on saving throws against these harmful
environmental effects.

##### Respirator

A respirator, or breath mask, is a portable device that allows an oxygen-breather to
survive in low-oxygen atmospheres. Although not suitable for use in outer-space, these
hands-free masks were essential equipment for exploring unknown planets. While
wearing a respirator, you have advantage on saving throws against poisons that rely on
being inhaled, and against environmental effects that rely on being inhaled, such as
noxious miasma.

#### Medical Supplies

```
Item Cost Weight
Medical Supplies
Antitoxin Kit 600 g 4 lbs.
Basic Poison 1,000 g 1 lbs.
Emergency Battery 70 g 5 lbs.
Trauma Kit 50 g 3 lbs.
Medpac 500 g 1 lbs.
Repair Kit 750 g 3 lbs.
```

##### Antitoxin Kit

An antitoxin kit is standard-issue Imperial equipment to those designated for
environments with hostile native xeno life that rely on poisons and venom to survive. A
kit has five charges. As an action, you can administer a charge of the kit to cure a target
of one poison affecting them or to give them advantage on saving throws against poison
for 1 hour. This provides no benefits to constructs.

##### Basic Poison

You can use the poison in this vial to coat one kinetic weapon or up to three pieces of
ammunition. Applying the poison takes an action. A creature hit by the poisoned
weapon or ammunition must make a DC 10 Constitution saving throw or take 1d4
poison damage. Once applied, the poison retains potency for 1 minute before drying.

##### Emergency Battery

All non-expendable machinations need recharging as they are used. The battery has ten
uses. As an action, you can expend one use of the kit to stabilize a construct or object
that has 0 hit points, without needing to make an Intelligence (Tech) check.

##### Trauma Kit

A common trauma kit can be stocked with chirurgeon equipment such as scalpels,
knives, and bonesaws, and contains spray-bandages, bone stabilizers, antiseptics, and
other essentials for the treatment of wounds. As an action, you can expend a use of the
kit to stabilize a creature that has 0 hit points, without needing to make a Wisdom
(Medicine) check. A trauma kit can be used to stabilize 5 times before it must be
restocked at its original cost.

##### Repair Kit

A repair kit included the basic tools needed to repair a droid after being damaged in
combat. The kit has three uses. As an action, you can expend one use of the kit to
restore 2d4+2 hit points to a droid or construct within 5 feet.

#### Utilities

```
Item Cost Weight
Utilities
Bedroll 10 g 7 lbs.
Blanket 50 g 3 lbs.
Chrono 100 g 1 lbs.
Distress beacon 500 g 8 lbs.
Field rations (1 day) 5 g 1 lbs.
Fusion cutter 25 g 2 lbs.
Glow lamp 10 g 2 lbs.
Grappling hook 50 g 4 lbs.
Heat generator 400 g 4 lbs.
Homing beacon 450 g 1 lbs.
Macrobinoculars 750 g 2 lbs.
Maglock boots 3,250 g 5 lbs.
Manacles 10 g 1 lbs.
Mess kit 20 g 1 lbs.
Mirror 50 g 1 lbs.
```

```
Ram, portable 40 g 35 lbs.
Restraining bolt 350 g 1 lbs.
Rope, 50 ft. (rolled) 20 g 2 lbs.
Shovel 7 g 5 lbs.
Tent, two-person 20 g 5 lbs.
```
##### Chrono

A chrono is a device that measures and keeps linear time. It can be worn on the wrist, or
on a chain attached to a piece of clothing.

##### Distress Beacon

A distress beacon is a bulky electronic box used to send your location quickly through
space to attempt to alert others that you are in distress and the coordinates of where
the distress beacon is located at. Although it can be helpful to be located, the distress
signal itself does not provide any information about its user, the people requesting help,
or the type of problem being encountered.

##### Field Rations (1 day)

Ration packs consist of dry foods suitable for extended travel, and are used when other
food is scarce. Each pack is divided into portions and can provide enough food for one
person per day.

##### Fusion Cutter

A fusion cutter is a handheld cutting tool popular among technicians. It cut through
almost any reinforced material, given enough time. The internal power cell supplies an
hour’s worth of continuous operation.

##### Glow Lamp

Glow lamps create a beam of light illuminating the area around you in bright light for a
20-foot radius and dim light for an additional 20 feet. The glow lamp lasts for 1 hour and
can be recharged by connecting to a power source or by replacing the power cell.

##### Grappling Hook

A grappling hook allows a user to climb or ascend large objects at your walking speed or
your climbing speed, whichever is faster. It can be mounted to a gun, belt, or elsewhere.
It has a 50-foot length.


##### Heat Generator

Heat generators are special devices typically worn on belts that function as a portable,
personal heat supply. Activating or deactivating the generator requires a bonus action
and, while active, you are adapted to cold climates, as described in chapter 5 of the
Dungeon Master’s Guide. The generator lasts for 1 hour and can be recharged by a
power source or replacing the power cell.

##### Homing Beacon

A homing beacon is a device used to track starships or any other entity being
transported. Homing beacons can’t be tracked through warp travel. Homing beacons
are small enough that they can easily be hidden inside a ship, or tucked into some
crevice on its exterior.

A homing beacon can be connected to a data-slate or similar recording device to receive
information of the beacon’s coordinates at any given time.

##### Macrobinoculars

Macrobinoculars are handheld viewing devices that allow users to observe distant
objects. Some models are able to see into space from the surface of a planet.

##### Maglock Boots

These boots can be used to magnetically lock onto a flat, metallic surface, such as a
ship’s hull. While maglocked, you can move up, down, and across metallic vertical
surfaces and upside down along metallic ceilings, while leaving your hands free.

While maglocked, you do not suffer the effects of being pushed away by effects of the
environment, such as the vacuum of space or powerful winds.

##### Manacles

These metal restraints can bind a Small or Medium creature. Escaping the manacles
requires a successful DC 20 Dexterity check. Breaking them requires a successful DC 20
Strength check. Each set of manacles comes with one key. Without the key, a creature
proficient with security kits can pick the manacles’ lock with a successful DC 15 Dexterity
check. Manacles have 15 hit points.

##### Mess Kit

This box contains a cup and simple cutlery. The box clamps together, and one side can


be used as a cooking pan and the other as a plate or shallow bowl.

##### Ram, Portable

You can use a portable ram to break down doors. When doing so, you gain a +5 bonus
on the Strength check. One other character can help you use the ram, giving you
advantage on this check.

##### Restraining Bolt

Restraining bolts are small, cylindrical devices that can be affixed to a construct in order
to limit its functions and enforce its obedience. When inserted, a restraining bolt
restricts the construct from any movement its master does not desire, and also forced it
to respond to signals produced by a hand-held control unit.

Installing a restraining bolt takes 1 minute. The construct must make a DC 13
Constitution saving throw. A hostile construct makes this save with advantage. On a
successful save, the restraining bolt overloads and is rendered useless. On a failed save,
the restraining bolt is correctly installed, and the control unit can be used to actively
control the construct. While the control unit is inactive, the construct can act freely but
it can not attempt to remove the restraining bolt.

#### Weapon & Armor Accessories

```
Item Cost Weight
Accessories
Bandolier 100 g 2 lbs.
Bipod 200 g 2 lbs.
Friction-Grip Gear 2,000 g 12 lbs.
Jetpack 4,500 g 20 lbs.
Remote Detonator 150 g 1 lbs.
Rocket Boots 2,500 g 3 lbs.
Stealth Field Generator 8,000 g 3 lbs.
Tracker Utility Vest 150 g 3 lbs.
```
##### Bandolier

A bandolier is worn across the chest. It has 12 slots that can each hold a single item that
weighs less than 2 lb, such as a combat knife, a fragmentation grenade, or a power cell.

##### Bipod


A bipod is a device mounted to a two-handed ranged weapon to offer increased stability
while prone. As an action, you can deploy or collapse the bipod. While deployed, you
ignore the Strength requirement on ranged weapons with the Strength property while
you are prone, and your speed is reduced to 0.

##### Friction-Grip Gear

A special set of gloves and boots that allow the wearer to stick to and climb surfaces.
While wearing these items, you gain the ability to move along vertical surfaces and
ceilings while leaving your hands free. You also gain a climbing speed equal to your
walking speed.

##### Jetpack

Jetpacks are personal aerial transportation devices that allow the operator to fly into
and through the air with great mobility. Activating or deactivating the jetpack requires a
bonus action and, while active, you have a flying speed of 30 feet. The jetpack lasts for 1
minute per quart of promethium (to a maximum of 10 minutes) and can be refueled as
an action.

##### Remote Detonator

A small handheld device with a single button, used to activate explosives. Over the
course of 1 minute, you can synchronize the detonator with a single explosive device,
such as a breaching charge, grenade, or mine. As an action, you can remotely detonate
the paired explosive up to a range of 300 feet.

##### Rocket Boots

Rocket boots are a form of rocket propulsion system affixed to a pair of boots instead of
being worn on the back like a standard jetpack. Activating or deactivating the boots
requires a bonus action and, while active, you have a flying speed of 20 feet. The rocket
boots last for 1 minute and can be recharged by a power source or replacing the power
cell.

##### Stealth Field Generator

Stealth field generators are special devices typically worn on belts that function as a
portable, personal cloaking device. Activating or deactivating the generator requires a
bonus action and, while active, you have advantage on Stealth checks that rely on sight.
The generator lasts for 1 minute and can be recharged by a power source or by
replacing the power cell. This effect ends early if you make an attack or cast a power.


##### Tracker Utility Vest

A utility vest is a sleeveless item of clothing that includes several evenly-distributed
pockets, popular among hunters, smugglers, and adventurers. The vest is made of
leathery, hide material to resist rips, corrosion and water. The wearer can carry up to 10
light items (up to 1 lb each) without increasing their total encumbrance.

## Tools

A tool helps you to do something you couldn’t otherwise do, such as craft or repair an
item, pick a lock, or slice into a computer. Your species, class, background, or feats give
you proficiency with certain tools, which lets you add your proficiency bonus to any
ability check you make using that tool. Tool use is not tied to a single ability, since
proficiency with a tool represents broader knowledge of its use.

```
Item Cost Weight
Misc. Tools
Herbalism Kit 250 g 2 lbs.
Navigator’s Tools 250 g 2 lbs.
Poisoner’s Kit 100 g 3 lbs.
Security Kit 250 g 2 lbs.
Vehicles (land, water, air, or space) — —
Torturer’s Kit 300 g 3 lbs.
Chirurgeon’s Tools 500 g 4 lbs.
Disguise Kit 300 g 2 lbs.
Forgery Kit 250 g 3 lbs.
```
##### Artisan’s Tools

These special tools include the items needed to pursue a craft or trade. The table shows
examples of the most common types of tools, each providing items related to a single
craft. Proficiency with a set of artisan’s tools lets you add your proficiency bonus to any
ability checks you make using the tools in your craft, or to checks made regarding your
craft. Each type of artisan’s tools requires a separate proficiency.

```
Item Cost Weight
Artisan’s Tools
Alchemist’s Supplies 500 g 9 lbs.
Brewer’s Supplies 200 g 9 lbs.
Calligrapher’s Supplies 100 g 5 lbs.
```

```
Carpenter’s Tools 80 g 6 lbs.
Cartographer’s Tools 150 g 6 lbs.
Cobbler’s Tools 50 g 5 lbs.
Cook’s Utensils 10 g 8 lbs.
Glassblower’s Tools 300 g 5 lbs.
Jeweler’s Tools 250 g 2 lbs.
Leatherworker’s Tools 50 g 5 lbs.
Mason’s Tools 100 g 8 lbs.
Painter’s Supplies 100 g 5 lbs.
Potter’s Tools 100 g 3 lbs.
Smith’s Tools 200 g 8 lbs.
Tinker’s Tools 500 g 10 lbs.
Weaver’s Tools 10 g 5 lbs.
Woodcarver’s Tools 10 g 5 lbs.
Hunter’s Tools 50 g 2 lbs.
Fisherman’s Tools 10 g 3 lbs.
Tattooist’s Tools 100 g 1 lbs.
Prospector’s Tools 150 g 3 lbs.
```
##### Disguise Kit

This pouch of cosmetics, hair dye, and small props lets you create disguises that change
your physical appearance, in addition to a tool that lets them mimic clothing. Proficiency
with this kit lets you add your proficiency bonus to any ability checks you make to create
a visual disguise.

##### Forgery Kit

This small box contains a variety of papers and parchments, pens and inks, seals and
sealing wax, gold and silver leaf, and other supplies necessary to create convincing
forgeries of physical documents. Proficiency with this kit lets you add your proficiency
bonus to any ability checks you make to create a physical forgery of a document.

##### Gaming Set

This item encompasses a wide range of game pieces, including dice and/or decks of
cards. A few common examples appear on the Tools table, but other kinds of gaming
sets exist. If you are proficient with a gaming set, you can add your proficiency bonus to
ability checks you make to play a game with that set. Each type of gaming set requires a
separate proficiency.

```
Item Cost Weight
```

```
Gaming Sets
Dice 1 g —
Regicide Set 100 g 1 lbs.
Playing Cards 5 g —
Chess 50 g 2 lbs.
```
##### Herbalism Kit

This kit contains a variety of instruments such as clippers, mortar and pestle, and
pouches and vials used by herbalists to create remedies and potions. Proficiency with
this kit lets you add your proficiency bonus to any ability checks you make to identify or
apply herbs.

##### Musical Instrument

Several of the most common types of musical instruments are shown on the table as
examples. If you have proficiency with a given musical instrument, you can add your
proficiency bonus to any ability checks you make to play music with the instrument.
Each type of musical instrument requires a separate proficiency.

```
Item Cost Weight
Musical Instrument
Bagpipes 300 g 6 lbs.
Drum 60 g 3 lbs.
Dulcimer 250 g 10 lbs.
Flute 20 g 1 lbs.
Lute 350 g 2 lbs.
Lyre 300 g 2 lbs.
Horn 30 g 2 lbs.
Pan Flute 120 g 2 lbs.
```
##### Navigator’s Tools

This set of instruments is used for navigation at land, sea, air, or space. Proficiency with
navigator’s tools lets you chart a ship’s course and follow navigation charts. In addition,
these tools allow you to add your proficiency bonus to any ability check you make to
avoid getting lost while traveling.

##### Poisoner’s Kit

A poisoner’s kit includes the vials, chemicals, and other equipment necessary for the
creation of poisons. Proficiency with this kit lets you add your proficiency bonus to any


ability checks you make to craft or use poisons.

##### Security Kit

A security kit includes the tools and electronic components necessary to bypass
electronic and mechanical locks. It includes sensor devices, a specialized commlink
designed to detect silent alarms, a small file, a set of lockpicks, a small mirror mounted
to an elongated handle, a set of narrow-bladed scissors, and a pair of pliers. Proficiency
with these tools lets you add your proficiency bonus to any ability checks you make to
disarm traps or open locks.

##### Tech Gadgets

```
Item Cost Weight
Tech Gadgets
Demolition’s kit 300 g 5 lbs.
Hacker’s kit 250 g 2 lbs.
Mechanic’s kit 100 g 4 lbs.
Armormech’s tools 150 g 8 lbs.
Armstech’s tools 150 g 5 lbs.
```
**_Demolition’s Kit._** This kit comes with the necessary wiring, components, gloves, and
tools to create and disarm explosives, from overloaded las guns to molotov cocktails.
These tools can only aid in the process of making explosives, so you would still need to
purchase or find other components to use as a base for the explosive. Proficiency with
these tools lets you add your proficiency bonus to any ability checks you make to create,
disarm, or manipulate explosives.
**_Hacker’s Kit._** Hackers use specialized computers and scramble keys, many built by
the hackers themselves, to eke out a living in the digital world. These devices are
carefully guarded and constantly modified and upgraded by the hacker, who rarely
discuss its specs except with like-minded individuals. Complex access codes and even
self-destruct mechanisms were often used to prevent a hacker’s computer from falling
into the wrong hands. Proficiency with this kit lets you add your proficiency bonus to
any ability checks you make to hack into computers or bypass security.
**_Mechanic’s Kit._** This kit contains all of the commonly required tools to make repairs
on constructs, such as ships, computers, and turrets. Proficiency with this kit lets you
add your proficiency bonus to any ability checks you make to perform repairs or install
upgrades to ships, ship weapons, ship hulls, and basic appliances and technology-based
basic devices.
**_Armormech’s Tools._** This kit contains tools used to fit armor, test durability, and
provide maintenance to armor, from leather to ceramite-enforced steel. Proficiency
with this kit lets you add your proficiency bonus to any ability checks you make to


repair, maintain, or modify armor.
**_Armstech’s Tools._** This kit contains tools used to clean weapons, adjust sights, and
provide maintenance to weapons, from lasguns to melta pistols. Proficiency with this kit
lets you add your proficiency bonus to any ability checks you make to repair, maintain,
or modify weapons

##### Chirurgeon’s Tools

This set of tools contains a set of calipers, a bonesaw, vials of anesthesia, scalpels, and
items needed to perform amputations, remove tumors or foreign objects, and applying
grafts. Proficiency in these tools allows you to add your proficiency bonus to your checks
to perform such operations.

##### Torturer’s Kit

This kit contains a wide range of blades, needles, chemicals, drugs, barbed hooks, neural
probes, thermal prods, and other essential tools for physical interrogation. Proficiency in
this kit allows you to add your proficiency bonus to your checks to interrogate creatures.

#### Trade Goods

Trade is an essential part of the galactic economy. Many traders make their living buying
and selling goods along interstellar routes that connect a sector’s major worlds.

A merchant may be chartered by an individual or a corporation to deliver goods to a
certain port, or move goods along a specified route. During times of war, opportunities
are abound in the shipping of ammunition and medical supplies. Some traders, seeking
to earn a quick profit, may resort to smuggling illegal or restricted cargo on behalf of
one of the galaxy’s many crime syndicates. The Trade Goods table shows the value of
commonly exchanged goods.

```

Animal, livestock 500 g

Art, common 100 g
Art, quality 1,000 g
Art, precious 10,000 g
Amasec, 1 gal 400 g
```

# Chapter 6: Customization Options

The combination of ability scores, race, class, and background defines your character’s
capabilities in the game, and the personal details you create set your character apart
from every other character. Even within your class and race, you have options to fine-
tune what your character can do. But this chapter is for players who—with the GM’s
permission—want to go a step further.

This chapter defines two optional sets of rules for customizing your character:
multiclassing and feats. Multiclassing lets you combine classes together, and feats are
special options you can choose instead of increasing your ability scores as you gain
levels. Your GM decides whether these options are available in a campaign.

## Multiclassing

Multiclassing allows you to gain levels in multiple classes. Doing so lets you mix the
abilities of those classes to realize a character concept that might not be reflected in
one of the standard class options.

With this rule, you have the option of gaining a level in a new class whenever you
advance in level, instead of gaining a level in your current class. Your levels in all your
classes are added together to determine your character level. For example, if you have
three levels in psyker and two in soldier, you’re a 5th-level character.

As you advance in levels, you might primarily remain a member of your original class
with just a few levels in another class, or you might change course entirely, never
looking back at the class you left behind. You might even start progressing in a third or
fourth class. Compared to a single-class character of the same level, you’ll sacrifice some
focus in exchange for versatility.

##### Multiclassing Example

Bob is playing a 4th-level soldier. When his character earns enough experience points to
reach 5th level, Bob decides that his character will multiclass instead of continuing to
progress as a fighter. Bob’s soldier has been spending a lot of time with Jim’s renegade,
and has even been doing some jobs on the side as a bounty hunter. Bob decides that his
character will multiclass into the renegade class, and thus his character becomes a 4th-
level soldier and 1st-level renegade (written as fighter 4/renegade 1).


When Bob’s character earns enough experience to reach 6th level, he can decide
whether to add another soldier level (becoming a soldier 5/renegade 1), another
renegade level (becoming a soldier 4/renegade 2), or a level in a third class, perhaps
dabbling in the technology thanks to a archaeotech dataslate he acquired (becoming a
soldier 4/renegade 1/mechnician 1).

#### Prerequisites

To qualify for a new class, you must meet the ability score prerequisites for both your
current class and your new one, as shown in the Multiclassing Prerequisites table. For
example, a soldier who decides to multiclass into the psyker class must have either
Strength or Dexterity and Wisdom or Charisma scores of 13 or higher. Without the full
training that a beginning character receives, you must be a quick study in your new
class, having a natural aptitude that is reflected by higher-than-average ability scores.

**Multiclassing Prerequisites
Class Ability Score Minimum**
Augmenticist Strength or Dexterity 13
Berserker Strength 13
Courser Strength or Dexterity 13, Intelligence 13
Crusader Strength 13 or Dexterity 13
Exorcist Constitution 13, Wisdom or Charisma 13
Mechnician Intelligence 13
Psyker Wisdom or Charisma 13
Renegade Dexterity 13
Soldier Strength or Dexterity 13
Sorcerer Wisdom or Charisma 13

#### Experience Points

The experience point cost to gain a level is always based on your total character level, as
shown in the Character Advancement table in chapter 1, not your level in a particular
class. So, if you are a psyker 6/soldier 1, you must gain enough XP to reach 8th level
before you can take your second level as a soldier or your seventh level as a psyker.

#### Hit Points and Hit Dice

You gain the hit points from your new class as described for levels after 1st. You gain the
1st-level hit points for a class only when you are a 1st-level character.


You add together the Hit Dice granted by all your classes to form your pool of Hit Dice. If
the Hit Dice are the same die type, you can simply pool them together. For example,
both the soldier and the exorcist have a d10, so if you are a soldier 5/exorcist 5, you
have ten d10 Hit Dice. If your classes give you Hit Dice of different types, keep track of
them separately. If you are a soldier 5/renegade 5, for example, you have five d10 Hit
Dice and five d8 Hit Dice.

#### Proficiency Bonus

Your proficiency bonus is always based on your total character level, as shown in the
Character Advancement table in chapter 1, not your level in a particular class. For
example, if you are a soldier 3/renegade 2, you have the proficiency bonus of a 5th-level
character, which is +3.

If a feature or feat allows you to forgo your proficiency bonus, you may only do so once.

#### Proficiencies

When you gain a level in a class other than your first, you gain only some of that class’s
starting proficiencies, as shown in the Multiclassing Proficiencies table.

**Multiclassing Proficiencies
Class Proficiencies Gained**
Augmenticist Light armor, claws, shortswords
Berserker Light armor, simple weapons, martial weapons
Courser Light armor, medium armor, simple weapons, martial weapons, one skill
from the class’s list
Crusader Light armor, medium armor, simple weapons, martial weapons, one skill
from the class’s list
Exorcist Light armor, medium armor, simple weapons, martial weapons
Mechnician Light armor, security kit, one skill from the class’s list, two tech gadgets
Psyker —
Renegade Light armor, simple weapons, two skills from the class’s list
Soldier Light armor, medium armor, simple weapons, martial weapons
Sorcerer —

#### Class Features


When you gain a new level in a class, you get its features for that level. A few features,
however, have additional rules when you’re multiclassing: Extra Attack, Superiority Die,
Unarmored Defense, and Force- or Tech-casting.

#### Extra Attack

If you gain the Extra Attack class feature from more than one class, the features don’t
add together. You can’t make more than two attacks with this feature unless it says you
do.

#### Unarmored Defense

If you already have the Unarmored Defense feature, you can’t gain it again from
another class.

#### Psycasting and Techcasting

Your capacity for psycasting and techcasting depends partly on your combined levels in
all your psycasting or techcasting classes and partly on your individual levels in those
classes. Once you have the psycasting or techcasting feature from more than one class,
use the rules below. If you multiclass but have the psycasting or techcasting feature
from only one class, you follow the rules as described in that class.

##### Powers Known

You determine what powers you know and can prepare for each class individually, as if
you were a single-classed member of that class. If you are a courser 4/psyker 3, for
example, you know 6 tech powers of no higher than 1st-level. As a 3rd-level psyker, you
know 11 force powers of no higher than 2nd-level.

Each power you know is associated with one of your classes, and you use the psycasting
or techcasting ability of that class when you cast the power.

##### Psyker and Tech Points

You determine your available force or tech points by adding together the amount given
by each class.

If you have both psyker and tech points, you keep your pools separate, and they can


only be used to fuel psychic or tech powers, respectively.

##### Max Power Level

When multiclassing, you determine your Max Power Level by first determining your
casting level total. To determine this total, you add up your total psycasting or
techcasting levels, and rounding down for the final result. Exorcists and coursers only
count as half of a psycasting or techcasting level. Finally, you consult the Multiclass Max
Power Level table below.

For example, if you have three levels in exorcist, which has 1.5 psycasting levels, and
three levels in psyker, which has 3 psycasting levels, your total psycasting level is 4.5,
rounded down to 4. You then compare that to the Multiclass Max Power Level table,
and see that as a 4th-level caster, your max power level is 2nd level.

If you have both psycasting and techcasting, you determine your Max Power Levels
separately, and they can only be used to cast psychic or tech powers, respectively.

**Multiclass Max Power Level
Caster Level Max Power Level**
1st-2nd 1st
3rd-4th 2nd
5th-6th 3rd
7th-8th 4th
9th-10th 5th
11th-12th 6th
13th-14th 7th
15th-16th 8th
17th-18th-19th-20th 9th

##### High-Level Casting

When determining the number of higher level powers you can cast before needing a
long rest, consult the rules for casting in the class in which you have the most levels.

## Feats

#### Alert

You are always on the lookout for danger, you gain the following benefits:


```
⦁ You gain a +5 bonus to initiative.
⦁ You can’t be surprised while you are conscious.
⦁ Other creatures don’t gain advantage on attack rolls against you as a result of
being unseen by you.
```
#### Athlete

You have undergone extensive physical training to gain the following benefits:
⦁ Increase your Strength or Dexterity score by 1, to a maximum of 20.
⦁ When you are prone, standing up uses only 5 feet of your movement.
⦁ Climbing doesn’t halve your speed.
⦁ You can make a running long jump or a running high jump after moving only 5
feet on foot, rather than 10 feet.

#### Actor

Skilled at mimicry and dramatics, you gain the following benefits:
⦁ Increase your Charisma score by 1, to a maximum of 20.
⦁ You have advantage on Deception and Performance checks when trying to pass
yourself off as a different person.
⦁ You can mimic the speech of another person or sounds made by other creatures.
You must have heard the person speaking, or heard the creature make the
sound, for at least 1 minute. A successful Insight check contested by your
Deception check allows a listener to determine that the effect is faked.

#### Ballistics Expert

Thanks to extensive training with firearms and marksmanship, you gain the following
benefits:

```
⦁ Being within 5 feet of a hostile creature does not impose disadvantage on your
ranged attack rolls.
⦁ You ignore the loading property on weapons with which you are proficient.
⦁ You can throw grenades up to double their distance.
```
#### Charger

When you use your action to Dash, you can use a bonus action to make one melee
weapon attack or to shove a creature.


If you move at least 10 feet in a straight line immediately before taking this bonus
action, you either gain a +5 bonus to the attack’s damage roll (if you chose to make a
melee attack and hit) or push the target up to 10 feet away from you (if you chose to
shove and you succeed).

#### Defensive Duelist

_Prerequisite: Dexterity 13 or higher_
When you are wielding a finesse weapon with which you are proficient and another
creature hits you with a melee attack, you can use your reaction to add your proficiency
bonus to your AC for that attack, potentially causing the attack to miss you.

#### Dual Wielder

You master fighting with two weapons, gaining the following benefits:
⦁ You gain a +1 bonus to AC while you are wielding a separate melee weapon in
each hand.
⦁ You can use two-weapon fighting even when the one-handed melee weapons
you are wielding aren’t light.
⦁ You can draw or stow two one-handed weapons when you would normally be
able to draw or stow only one, and you can reload weapons without needing a
free hand.

#### Dungeon Delver

Alert to the hidden traps and secret doors found in many dungeons, you gain the
following benefits:
⦁ When you roll a Hit Die to regain hit points, the minimum number of hit points
you regain from the roll equals twice your Constitution modifier (minimum of 2).
⦁ You have advantage on Wisdom (Perception) and Intelligence (Investigation)
